Zhejiang Province Issues Public Bonds

Please Name It Disaster Relief

The All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association sent a telegram saying: "Mr. Chiang Kai-shek, Zhejiang is suffering from severe drought. From the plum rain season to the beginning of autumn, there has been no rain for a hundred days. Rivers have dried up, and fields have cracked. Late rice has not been planted, and seedlings have withered. Potatoes, yams, melons, and beans have also been scorched to death. Rice prices have soared, more than doubling the normal price. The severity of the disaster is unprecedented in a century. Since the 12th year of the Republic, Zhejiang Province has suffered from repeated disasters, including floods. There has been almost no year without a disaster, and no disaster that has not been severe. The granaries have long been depleted. Now, we are suffering from an unprecedented drought, just like a long-term illness or serious injury, with pain and scars being created again. Recently, incidents of robbing rice and families starving to death have been repeatedly reported. Hunger-stricken people from Ningyan Binhai Huangwan Baolang and other places are forming groups to sell surplus salt in exchange for a few liters of rice, resulting in the tragic incident of tax police shooting and killing many people. The salt people, in order to eke out a living, do not care about being severely punished. Carrying loads on their shoulders, they still continue to travel the roads. Tragedies may not be difficult to see again. In addition, hooligans are inciting people in desolate areas. The future is uncertain, and hidden worries are growing. Fellow Zhejiang natives in Shanghai, in view of the seriousness of the disaster, have repeatedly gathered to discuss the establishment of the All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, hoping to do their best to help their fellow citizens. We have heard that Zhejiang Province is issuing 20 million in public bonds, and representatives such as Chen Qinshi, Yu Qiaqing, and Wang Xiaolai have been elected to petition the provincial government to use these public bonds for emergency relief, namely, to organize work relief and restore water conservancy throughout the province, but we have not received a clear answer. At a time when the people are impoverished and have no surplus funds, they can no longer bear this huge burden. If it is used for disaster prevention and relief, as a temporary expedient, although it is a policy of drinking poison to quench thirst, at a time when both public and private resources are exhausted, the people should understand the government's unavoidable distress of accumulating debts and sympathize with them. If it is used to make up for the shortage of government expenses and to carry out unnecessary construction projects to beautify politics and disregard the people's hardships, the people of Zhejiang, even if they are weak, will swear to do their best to oppose it. This public bond is currently under review by the Ministry of Finance. We respectfully ask you to take care of your hometown and to preside over the matter. Please send a telegram to the Ministry of Finance to amend the public bond regulations, naming it a disaster relief public bond and ensuring that it is used for relief and water conservancy construction, so that the remaining disaster victims can receive practical benefits. We urgently submit this petition and hope that you will take note of it. Furthermore, our association was just established on a cold day and has not yet elected standing committee members and chairmen. We hereby state this together. All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, K., Qiao. (The telegram to the Ministry of Finance is omitted)."

The City Chamber of Commerce Telegraphs the Ministry of Communications to Order the Shanghai Post Office to Use Domestic Coal 120

Recovering the Leakage of More Than 20,000 Yuan in Diesel Fuel Every Year

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing yesterday, saying: "We received a letter from the Coal Industry Association on the 17th of this month, stating: 'According to a letter from our member, Shanxi Coal Industry Company, the International Trade Bureau has repeatedly announced that the trade deficit index is gradually increasing. All Chinese people are heartbroken and are planning ways to promote domestic products. It is not too late to mend the fold after the sheep are lost. We believe that the self-built building of the Shanghai Postal Administration has heating equipment. When the building was completed, coal was used as fuel for more than two years. Later, the original intention was suddenly changed, and imported diesel fuel was used instead. The annual consumption reached more than 30,000 yuan. This trivial matter may not have been noticed by the authorities of the Ministry of Communications, but if small leaks are not stopped, they will become rivers and seas. A single spark can start a prairie fire. It is estimated that there are no less than 200 tall buildings in Shanghai, and 99% of them use coal. Even those that previously used diesel fuel have now switched to coal, such as the Jianghai Customs Building, the British HSBC Bank, and other bank apartments. The fact that they have switched from diesel fuel to coal proves that domestic coal is superior to diesel fuel in terms of both efficiency and economy. Now, the people of the country are loudly calling for the use of domestic products, but government agencies are instead monopolized by foreigners and do not promote them. However, sovereignty ultimately belongs to our government, so we deeply hope that our government agencies can promote them first, setting an example so that the people will follow and obey, thereby strengthening the country's power. Moreover, domestic coal is now abundant in the market and is sold at low prices. The bureau can take this opportunity to use domestic coal in order to recover its rights and interests. Our company, having learned of the previous situation, cannot remain silent. We know that your association is a group of our coal industry and is enthusiastic about promoting domestic coal, so we dare to request that you forward a letter to the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce to submit to the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Industry for review and verification. Please issue separate orders to the Shanghai Postal Administration to comply with the above and improve the promotion of domestic coal. The national economy and the people's livelihood will benefit greatly.' According to this, we have found that domestic coal is currently in a competitive relationship with foreign coal, so the market price is very low. If we can abandon diesel fuel and switch to domestic coal, we can save a lot of money. We can both promote domestic products and plug the leak. It is truly killing two birds with one stone. Accordingly, we request that your association approve the forwarding of this letter to the two ministries of communications and industry, and quickly issue separate orders to the Shanghai Postal Administration to switch to domestic coal in order to show its promotion and maintain domestic coal. This will be a public service." "We have found that the Postal Administration is a state agency and has the responsibility to promote domestic products. Diesel fuel is currently used and is purely foreign goods. Our country does not yet have a domestically produced substitute. Heating equipment has domestic coal available, and the bureau should not switch to diesel fuel, which would promote the sales of imported goods. The sales of this item are said to reach more than 30,000 yuan a year, which is not a very large amount, but it is related to international perception and public opinion. If it is not corrected, then the so-called 'the wind blows over the grass, and the grass bends,' and 'the law is implemented from above' will all be in vain. How can we reverse the corruption of morals and customs? It is reasonable to telegraph your ministry for review and verification, and to order the Shanghai Bureau to correct this, as a public service. Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, K., Xiao."

Xu Jigong Passes Away in Xiamen, Friends in Shanghai Will Hold a Memorial Service 123

Mr. Xu Jigong, former chairman of the Overseas Chinese Federation, was born in Taiwan. Twenty years ago, unable to bear the pain of Taiwan's loss, he abandoned his family and returned to the motherland, engaging in business in Shanghai, such as the Great China Record Company and the Tobacco Company. Around 1919 and 1920, he and overseas Chinese returning from Nanyang in Shanghai, such as Xie Bietian and Li Denghui, established the Overseas Chinese Federation, making many achievements. In 1929, he was elected as the chairman of the association. When the Shanghai War broke out, Mr. Xu witnessed the lack of food and salaries for the 19th Route Army. He and Zhu Qinglan, Zheng Hongnian, Xu Shiying, and others initiated the Overseas Chinese National Salvation Economic Committee to raise funds from overseas Chinese to help the military. Later, in view of the importance of publicity, he and Liu Shimu, Xie Nanguang, and others organized the Hualian News Agency to publicize the anti-Japanese work at home and abroad. Last year, the Overseas Chinese Federation was reorganized, and Mr. Xu gave the position of chairman to Chen Wulie, a Chinese from Thailand in Shanghai, and he himself became the vice chairman. This spring, after the Fujian Incident was quelled, Mr. Xu listened to the persuasion of friends and went to Xiamen to promote the construction of the ten counties in southern Fujian, dividing them into autonomous regions for returned overseas Chinese. He temporarily resided in Xiamen. The bad news came that Mr. Xu suffered a cerebral hemorrhage (commonly known as a stroke) in his apartment in Xiamen earlier this month. It only took about fifteen minutes, and he passed away. It is reported that after his wife and others received the news, they took a boat to Xiamen a few days ago to attend the funeral. They plan to transport the coffin to Shanghai for burial. His friends in Shanghai also plan to hold a memorial service to express their grief.

Page 12

Responsible Person of the Garrison Department Discusses the Drug Situation in Shanghai 126

Overview of Drug Cases　　Statistics on Compulsory Rehabilitation

Methods of Drug Rehabilitation　　Personal Views

Red pills and morphine have an enormous impact on individual happiness and national health. Yesterday, a reporter from the Central News Agency, in order to understand the drug rehabilitation situation in this city, specifically visited the Longhua Command Headquarters and interviewed the responsible personnel of the department. They were informed of the recent drug rehabilitation situation in Shanghai as follows:

(Overview of Drug Cases) The prohibition of drugs in this city has always been taken very seriously. Since Chairman Chiang issued the regulations strictly prohibiting highly addictive drugs, the implementation has been swift and effective. In the first month of the implementation of the regulations, June, the Public Security Bureau arrested 435 people for compulsory rehabilitation. The numbers gradually decreased in July and August. However, on average, more than seven criminals are apprehended each month and are all sent by the Public Security Bureau to this headquarters for legal processing. According to the law, anyone who smokes or takes drugs is sent to the drug rehabilitation center for a limited period of compulsory rehabilitation. Those who are proven by the drug rehabilitation center to have completely quit are released on bail and may be summoned for investigation if they are involved in another case in the future. These types of drug offenders are the most numerous. Next are drug traffickers, followed by those who provide lighting for others to smoke red pills or administer morphine injections. Next are transporters, and finally, manufacturers. Those offenders whose circumstances are serious are subject to Article 14 of the Regulations Strictly Prohibiting Highly Addictive Drugs, which provides for a reduction of one-half of the death penalty, and a change to imprisonment for a term of no less than twelve years, as a show of leniency. In the past month, although drug offenders have continued to be sent in a steady stream, more than nine out of ten are smokers, and there are very few traffickers and manufacturers. This is something to be very gratifying to the society.

(Statistics on Compulsory Rehabilitation) After the command headquarters began handling drug cases, it was approved by the municipal government to allocate funds to set up a temporary drug rehabilitation center opposite the headquarters. Recently, the statistics compiled by the center for last month were reviewed. Among the 553 drug offenders who underwent rehabilitation at the center, 462 were male and 91 were female. In terms of age, 3 were under 20 years old, 141 were between 20 and 30 years old, 224 were between 31 and 40 years old, 134 were between 41 and 50 years old, and 51 were over 51 years old. Most of them are in their prime. It is truly unknown what afflicts them that they would waste their useful years on drugs. In addition, in terms of occupation, 294 were laborers, 151 were merchants, 23 were farmers, 8 were from the academic world, 3 were soldiers, and 74 were unemployed. However, some of the employed have already lost their jobs due to drug use. As for the time it took to break the drug addiction in the center, 499 people did so within ten days, 30 within twelve days, 17 within fourteen days, and 4 within sixteen days. Three people had their rehabilitation stopped due to serious illness.

(Methods of Drug Rehabilitation) Most hospitals use opium substitutes for drug rehabilitation, gradually reducing the dosage through (tapering). However, because the toxins in the blood are not eliminated, the addiction may return soon. After research by the Health Bureau, the headquarters' drug rehabilitation has changed to using (autologous serum). The method involves applying a mixture of pure ammonia and 10% camphor oil to the chest of the drug offender. After about half an hour, several small blisters will appear on the area. Use a warm towel compress, and after a considerable amount of time, after the small blisters have merged, the toxic fluid inside the blisters is extracted with a sterilized syringe and injected under the skin of the offender. In this way, the person undergoing rehabilitation will feel refreshed after one blistering injection. If the drug addiction is deep and there are still signs of withdrawal the next day, a second or third blistering injection can be given using the same method. After the third time, no one has failed to quit. In short, the regulations issued by Chairman Chiang this time impose severe penalties on those who traffic and manufacture drugs, while those who smoke or take drugs are sent for medical rehabilitation for the first time, released on bail, without imprisonment or fines. This combination of leniency and severity is enough to make the people fear the government's power and be grateful for its kindness. Therefore, since its implementation, the results have been remarkable. Currently, the only free drug rehabilitation hospital is the Municipal Drug Rehabilitation Center opposite this headquarters. However, due to financial constraints, it cannot accept many people who voluntarily seek rehabilitation. Currently, more than 200 people have registered, and more are coming in an endless stream. It is hoped that philanthropists will continue to establish more centers so that poor citizens can all escape their dark fate. As for the Special District Court of this city, drug offenders involving highly addictive drugs are still dealt with in accordance with the Opium Suppression Law. Will drug offenders who smoke red pills and morphine regard the concessions as a haven? Whether the drug prohibition efforts in the concessions will be effective, and whether the drug prohibition affairs in the interior will not be affected by the concessions are matters that we and the concession authorities should pay close attention to.

Wang Xinshan, Assassin of Jin Menggen, Sentenced to Death 127

Wang Repeatedly Proclaimed His Innocence

He Has Declared an Appeal

Jin Menggen, a local from Zhoujiaqiao, who ran the Shunxingyuan teahouse in the Shanghai West area and also worked as an inspector at the Shenxin Yarn Factory, left the Zhoujiaqiao teahouse at around 5:00 AM on April 30th of this year, intending to return to his home on Dajin Road. A public trial was held by Criminal Court President Liu Enrong, and the deceased's wife, Jin Liu, and Jin Bao, requested justice. Wang Xinshan repeatedly proclaimed his innocence. At 2:00 PM, Judge Liu, accompanied by Assessors Shao Qinzhi and Yang Qianchang, specially opened the Third Tribunal to announce the verdict. Wang Xinshan, who was in custody, was brought to the case and briefly questioned before the verdict was announced in court: Wang Xinshan was found guilty of premeditated murder and sentenced to death. Wang did not accept the verdict and declared an appeal in court. The judge granted the appeal and instructed him to submit the reasons for the appeal in accordance with the law. After the sentence was announced, he was ordered to be returned to custody to await further instructions.

A Large Rat Runs Under the Altar of the God of Wealth, Temple Collapses 128

Shi Jinlin Sees Rat Enter Temple

Injured Along with the Temple Keeper

Next door to Hongyuan Paint Shop, No. 6, intersection of Lihong Bridge Pier, East Hanbi Li Road, and Dixiwei Road, Hongkou, is a Temple of the God of Wealth. Its incense has been quite prosperous. All affairs of the temple are maintained by the temple keeper Dong Anlin. However, the temple has already decayed, and is eroded by incense smoke daily. During winds and floods, it looks like it will collapse. Yesterday at 1:00 PM, the owner of Hongyuan Paint Shop, Shi Jinlin of Shaoxing, was idling near the temple when he suddenly saw a large rat running under the altar of the God of Wealth. Shi thought such a large rat was a novelty, so he walked into the temple with the temple keeper to take a look. As they were talking, a loud noise suddenly came from the roof, and then the entire house, including the roof tiles and walls, collapsed at the same time. Shi and Dong were unable to escape and were buried in the bricks and tiles. A newspaper vendor woman near the temple was also affected. Fortunately, the guards nearby arrived and reported to the police station, who notified the fire brigade. The fire brigade immediately sent an ambulance to rescue the three from the rubble and took them to Tongren Hospital for treatment. However, Shi Jinlin died from his injuries before arriving at the hospital and was sent to the coroner's office for an autopsy. Dong Anlin's injuries were also serious. The newspaper vendor woman's injuries were minor and not life-threatening.

Fish Vendor Kills Man with a Punch Over Crab Dispute 129

Yu Guilin Lashes Out with His Fist

Zhou Heshang Dies from Serious Injuries

Yu Guilin, 34 years old, from Minhang, has been transporting fresh fish, crabs, shrimps, etc., to Shanghai for sale at Yongtai Fish Shop, No. 46 Xiaodongmen Street, French Concession, to earn a meager profit and make a living. Yesterday morning, Yu transported several baskets of live crabs from the countryside to Shanghai and put them in front of Yongtai Fish Shop for sale. Zhou Heshang, 32 years old, from Haining, had a fresh fish stall at No. 103 Huanghe Road, French Concession, and made a living by selling fresh fish. At 5:15 AM yesterday morning, Zhou went to Xiaodongmen to pick up goods from his home. He bought crabs from Yu, weighing them and calculating the price at 3.2 yuan. Later, Zhou intended to buy another basket, but because there were too many dead crabs inside, he was afraid that he would not be able to sell them and would lose money, so he wanted to pick out some of them. Yu refused, and the two began to quarrel. Without saying a word, Yu punched Zhou with a fist, hitting his left rib. Zhou squatted on the ground, unable to get up. People were shocked and gathered around to watch. Chinese police officer No. 631 from the French Concession Police Station arrived and arrested the assailant Yu Guilin. He brought the injured person to the Xiaodongmen Police Station. The police chief ordered Zhou to be sent to Renji Hospital for treatment and had Yu detained for investigation. However, Zhou died from his injuries. The hospital notified the police station, who sent investigators to transport the body to Tongren Yuandan Hall for an autopsy. Zhou Huang, the deceased's wife, and witnesses Wu Hongchang (Yongtai Fish Shop worker) and Yang Aqi (fish vendor) were summoned. At noon, the case was reported to the Second Special District Court. Prosecutor Wang Ren, accompanied by a forensic doctor and clerk, arrived at the hall to examine the body. Officer Zhang Chunsheng reported the case, and investigator Xu Jialin brought the accused assailant to the case. The official questioned the deceased's wife, the accused, and the witnesses. It was ruled that Zhou Heshang had died from internal injuries caused by being beaten. The body was handed over to Zhou Huang for burial. The accused was handed over to the police department for interrogation.

Teng Tom, Who Had Obtained Portuguese Nationality, Commits Suicide 130

Friends Borrowed Money and Did Not Return It, Damaging His Reputation Instead

Teng Held a Party with Singers Before Committing Suicide

At 12:00 AM the night before last, a man wearing a suit and a young woman checked into room 107 of the Dadong Hotel at No. 94 Xixinqiao Street, French Concession, agreeing to a room rate of 1.2 yuan. The man identified himself as He Chongru, 32 years old, from Guangdong. As usual, the hotel servant brought tea and water. Suddenly, the guest ordered the servant to call singers from the street to the room to sing and have fun, and then closed the door to sleep. At 8:00 AM yesterday morning, the young woman got up and went out alone. At 11:00 AM, the guest ordered the servant to buy a plate of soup dumplings. He ate alone in the room. Unexpectedly, when eating the sixth soup dumpling, the guest could not support himself and fell to the ground, foaming at the mouth. The servant was shocked and reported to the accounting office and the French Concession Police Station. Investigator Liu Dianlong was dispatched to investigate. The guest was already dead. A Portuguese citizen certificate was found in his pocket, with the name Teng Tom, etc. Liu went to the Portuguese Consulate to inquire and learned that the deceased was not He Chongru, but Teng Tom, who ran the Dechang Jewelry Store on Broadway, Hongkou. They went to the store to investigate his family. It was said that a friend of Teng's had borrowed more than 30,000 yuan from him, but not only did he not return it, but he also published articles damaging his reputation. Therefore, Teng was angry and committed suicide by taking poison. Afterwards, a clerk from the store arrived at the scene to inspect and confirmed the details. The body was then transported to a funeral home for storage.

Executive Yuan Approves Chamber of Commerce's Implementation of Cotton Regulation Act 133

Date of Implementation Announced by Central Government

Sheng She reports that the Executive Yuan replied to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday: A substitute declaration has been made. In addition, the Chinese Cotton Mill Federation and others have sent a telegram requesting that the date of implementation of the Provisional Regulations on Prohibiting Water Adulteration and the detailed rules of implementation be announced immediately. Three departments, namely the Ministry of Commerce, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Justice, and the Ministry of Administration, were convened, and the National Economic Council was also invited to hold a joint meeting to review the case. According to the review report, (1) the standards for water adulteration stipulated in the regulations were approved by the Central Political Conference and passed by the Legislative Yuan and should not be changed again, (2) the officially set adulteration standards will be determined by the competent authority when they are implemented in the future, but there should be no bias against any aspect of the merchants, (3) the implementation of origin inspection will be conducted jointly by the Ministry of Industry and the National Economic Council, (4) the date of implementation should be determined and announced by the Central Government after considering the circumstances and formulating detailed rules of implementation. In addition to sending a letter to the National Economic Council for reference and informing the Ministry of Industry, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Justice, and the Ministry of Administration, it is hoped that you will take note of this approval.

Yan Luqing's Appeal Case Concluded 134

Sentencing Scheduled for the 25th of This Month

Lawyer Yan Luqing was previously involved in a case where he allegedly demanded compensation of 60,000 yuan from the families of suspects Zhang Zuming, Zhuang Jimeng, Wang Lianyou, and Tang Qingyue in the robbery case of Xue Mailuo Accounting Firm. The French Concession Police Department prosecuted him in the Second Special District Court on suspicion of extortion. As a result, he was sentenced to one year and six months in prison and fined 800 yuan. Because Yan did not accept the judgment, he filed an appeal with the Third Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court. The High Court approved the appeal and scheduled a hearing for 4:00 PM yesterday, to be heard by a collegial panel consisting of Court President Guo Dezhang, Sun Honglin, Fan Peien, and Chief Prosecutor Zhao Shibei. Lawyer Fei Xizhen represented the Police Department in court. The appellant Yan Luqing, accompanied by his lawyers Dong Kang, Shi Liang, and Peng Qi, appeared in court. Witnesses Zhao Zhongdi, Sun Zuji (lawyer), Pan Hongding (Shanghai Municipal Committee Member of Qingdong High Bank), Huang Xingzhong, and interested parties Zhou Jinggeng and others were summoned. After the court was convened, the appellant Yan Luqing was first summoned to the case, questioned about his age, origin, and residence. Then, he was asked: "The Second Special District Court sentenced you to two years and six months in prison and fined you 800 yuan for the extortion case. What are your reasons for appealing?" He replied, "The original judgment was wrong and was completely based on the words of the witnesses. Those witnesses are all their shop assistants, relatives, friends, lawyers, etc. The testimonies they provided are all contradictory." He was asked, "Did you instruct Tang Wenshou, the family member of Tang Qingyue, to ask for 2,000 yuan for a private settlement?" He replied, "No." He was asked, "Was it not you and Zhou Jinggeng who delivered the money to you by Pan Hongding at Sun Zuji's law firm?" He replied, "At 12:30 PM on June 21st, Zhou Jinggeng went to pick it up alone. I was having lunch in the Western restaurant and was not at the scene. The manager of the Western restaurant testified during the first instance." He was asked, "Have you been to Ruichangshun and Zhuangyuanda?" He replied, "Zhao Zhongdi invited me to see them, meaning that Zhang Zuming and Zhuang Jimeng were shopkeepers and had professions and would not be robbers, so I went to see them." He was asked, "Did you ask Zhang Zuyin of Ruichangshun for 60,000 yuan for a private settlement?" He replied, "No, that's completely wrong." He was asked, "Did you go to Zhuangyuanda immediately after leaving Ruichangshun?" He replied, "Zhao Zhongdi also invited me. I went with Zhou Jinggeng, Zhou's nephew Zhou Juren, and Zhao." He was asked, "Did you ask Zhang Yuquan of Zhuangyuanda for 60,000 yuan for a private settlement?" He replied, "No." He was asked, "Did you ask Sun Zuji for 6,000 yuan when he went to Xiahui Road to find a guarantor?" He replied, "I came out of the police station and returned to the office. I ran into him on the road in a car. He said that I asked him for money, which is completely fabricated." He was asked, "Did you ask Sun Zuji to exchange conditions when he called?" He replied, "Sun called to ask me for help. I replied that a private lawsuit was possible, but a public lawsuit was not possible, but I did not call him." He was asked, "Sun Zuji and Pan Hongding said that Pan put 2,000 yuan in banknotes on the counter of Sun's law firm, and you took it away?" He replied, "I have never been to Sun Zuji's law firm." He was asked, "Apart from the inconsistent testimonies of the witnesses, do you have any other reasons?" He replied, "My witnesses testified that I was eating in the Western restaurant." The official summoned witness Zhao Zhongdi to the case, who stated that he was 29 years old, from Wuxi, and lived at No. 1004 Broadway, and had no relationship with lawyer Yan. On June 17th, he went to the French Concession Police Station for Zhang Zuming and was detained overnight. The next morning, when he left the police station, lawyer Yan and Zhou Jinggeng greeted him when he hired a car in front of the door. I took their car to the Xue Mailuo office first, and then to Ruichangshun. I made three phone calls inside, and they were talking outside. I vaguely heard a few loud words, but I didn't know the details. Later, Zhou Jinggeng wanted Zhang Zuyin to go to Zhuangyuanda, but Zhang refused, so he asked me to accompany him. When we arrived at Zhuangyuanda, I went to the accounting room, and they were in the reception room. I don't know what they said. At first, I told Yan and Zhou in the police station that Zhang Zuming and others were old shopkeepers who wouldn't be robbers. If they didn't believe me, they could go and see their shops. The official summoned Zhou Jinggeng, who stated that he was a comprador at Xue Mailuo Accounting Firm. On June 18th, Zhao Zhongdi invited him to go with lawyer Yan to see Ruichangshun and Zhuangyuanda. We first went to Ruichangshun, and Zhao greeted him and introduced him to a big man. I told him that 6,000 yuan had been robbed on May 13th last year and that 12,000 yuan had been robbed this time. I did not mention asking for 60,000 yuan for a private settlement. Later, at Zhuangyuanda, I sat down in the reception room. After they served tea, I wanted to call my own writing room, but I couldn't get through, so I went back. At that time, I saw Zhang Yuquan, Zhuang Duanmeng's father-in-law, who was an old friend of lawyer Yan. When I left, Zhao Zhongdi sent me to the door and left. Lawyer Sun Zuji called me to pick up Tang Qingyue's 2,000 yuan. Later, Tang was declared not guilty and wrote a letter asking to return the money. I have returned the money in full, and there is a receipt as proof. According to the testimony of witnesses Sun Zuji, Pan Hongding, Huang Xingzhong, etc., the situation at that time was the same as that provided in the first instance and published in various newspapers, so it will not be repeated here. After the witnesses were questioned, the court ordered the opening of arguments. The three lawyers Dong, Shi, and Peng, hired by the appellant, and the Police Department's lawyer debated. The prosecutor then expressed his opinion. The court announced the end of the debate and scheduled the verdict for 2:00 PM on the 25th. When the court adjourned, the clock struck seven.

Fruit Vendor Sentenced for Wielding Knife 135

Sentenced to One Month in Prison

Zhu Yongyu, from Yangzhou, runs a fruit stall near Yulin Road. At around 8:00 AM the day before yesterday, Xu Degong, from Funing, who sells gardenias, passed by. Zhu took a gardenia from him and gave him a copper coin. Because he thought it was too little, they quarreled. At that time, Du Linggao, from Jiangbei, mediated and asked him to increase the amount. Zhu became furious, thinking that he was deliberately interfering, and spoke harshly. A fight broke out. Zhu was no match for him and took a fruit knife from the stall and stabbed Du in the face and shoulder twice, causing him to fall to the ground and bleed profusely. Chinese police officer Pan Yunlong heard the alarm and arrested Zhu, along with the murder weapon, and took him to the Yulin Road Police Station for detention. The injured person was taken to Shengxin Hospital for treatment. Fortunately, his injuries were not serious. After the doctor bandaged him, he was discharged from the hospital. Zhu was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court yesterday morning. 工部局 lawyer Li Zhishan described the previous situation and presented the murder weapon. Du Linggao and Xu Dehua testified about what happened. Questioned the defendant, whose testimony was evasive. Assessor Wu Zehan sentenced Zhu Yongyu to three months in prison, and the murder weapon was confiscated.

Newspaper Vendors Scramble to Open Packages and Get Newspapers at the Station 137

The Railway Bureau Resolutely Cracks Down

The Central News Agency reports that when various Shanghai newspapers arrive at the Nanjing Xiaguan Station by the Beijing-Shanghai Railway train every day, they are delivered by the on-board post office near the station. As a result, newspaper vendors scramble to enter the platform and open the packages themselves to get the newspapers, causing chaos and throwing the packaging paper all over the ground. This has greatly affected the order and cleanliness of the station. The Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration has sent a letter to the Shanghai Daily Association, informing the Nanjing managers of each newspaper that in the future, newspapers should not be unpacked and distributed within the station platform. The Daily Association replied that it had been resolved at a meeting that in addition to sending letters to the Nanjing branches of each member newspaper, they would send personnel to the station to receive the newspapers and would not unpack and distribute the newspapers within the platform. The Railway Administration was requested to order the police and stationmaster to take measures to crack down on this. This would not only maintain order at the station, but also allow the newspaper recipients of each branch to carry the newspapers out of the station and unpack them for distribution. It is hoped that this will be taken into consideration. After receiving this letter, the Railway Bureau immediately ordered the Traffic Department and the Police Department to designate a nearby location outside the station as a place for unpacking and distributing newspapers. However, Nanjing newspaper vendors threatened not to distribute newspapers. It is reported that the Railway Bureau has decided to persist in this measure in order to maintain order within the station.

Taikoo Dismantles the Poyang Steamer, Workers in All Departments Receive Severance Pay 140

The British-owned Taikoo Company's Yangtze River steamer Poyang is to be dismantled due to its age. However, the workers in various departments of the steamer, including tallymen, midshipmen, stokers, sailors, and stewards, had repeatedly negotiated against this due to livelihood concerns. Now, after a long period of negotiation, a complete resolution has been reached by both sides. A total of more than twenty tallymen will be paid wages up to the middle of September. In addition, they will receive severance pay equivalent to two months' wages including promotions. As for the midshipmen, who are employees of the comprador, the comprador will be responsible for handling their severance. The company will be responsible for the severance of the stokers, sailors, and stewards.

New Organization of the Datong Music Society 143

Teaching Guqin and Pipa

Editing National Music Magazine

The Datong Music Society in this city has cultivated a large number of professional talents in ancient music over the years. Since participating in the performance of ancient music during the Confucius birthday celebration this year, it has gained considerable social recognition. Therefore, the number of people seeking to study at the society has increased. Therefore, the society has expanded its operations. In addition to the Guqin class taught by Zheng Jinwen, the director of music affairs of the society, and the Pipa class taught by Wei Zhongle, the deputy director of music affairs, special classes such as Konghou and Da Se have been added, which are all available for students to choose from. Tuition fees remain the same: individual teaching is four yuan per month, and general class teaching is two yuan per month, which is truly a unique opportunity for those who study national music. (For regulations, please send one cent for postage to the society at No. 36 Songshan Road for a copy). National music is where the national spirit of our country lies. Now, it has deteriorated to the extreme. In recent years, after various promotions, it has slightly improved. However, without accurate publications, it is inevitable that everyone will go their own way, like scattered sand. It is still feared that it will be difficult to sustain. For this reason, in addition to organizing musical scores and manufacturing musical instruments, the society has also established a department for editing national music magazines. The content is divided into four categories: music theory, musical instruments, music songs, and music dances, plus a literature section. The authors are all contemporary celebrities, and the materials are very rich, which is truly an indispensable move in today's national music scene.

Rent Reduction Committee Urges Quick Determination of Rent Reduction Standards 145

A Response to the Memorandum of the Real Estate Association

The Shanghai Municipal Rent Reduction Committee recently stated that the rent reduction issue has not been resolved, which has greatly affected the social economy and market commerce. Therefore, it was resolved to explain the reasons in detail and appeal to the Executive Yuan and the Shanghai Municipal Government to quickly set rent reduction standards to resolve disputes. It is learned that the document has been drafted by Li Shirui, a design member of the committee, and has been approved and issued by the committee. The original text lists various reasons in great detail. Therefore, an excerpt is provided below to urge the quick determination of rent reduction standards for implementation. Rents in this city are expensive. The income of citizens who work hard is more than half taken by landlords. As a result, the necessities of clothing, food, housing, and transportation cannot be met. Various grievances have been stated on record. It has been half a year, and no clear order has been received to resolve the issue. Although there are a few enlightened landlords who automatically reduce rents, those who want to be unrestrained still impose excessive taxes and demand strict collections. Landlords and tenants confront each other, and lawsuits continue. This is truly a widespread and profound disaster in this city, just as severe as the severe drought in the countryside. After repeated consideration, the committee believes that if the rent reduction issue is not resolved for a day, not only will this city become increasingly depressed and gradually collapse, but its impact will affect the national finance and even the overall commodity market and production business, and the landlords will also suffer the same consequences without escape. The committee's request for rent reduction is by no means to represent only the one-sided interests of tenants, nor is it to exploit landlords for self-enrichment, just as the Real Estate Association said, "Being in the same boat during a storm, we should understand each other." (1) The population of this city is said to be 3.4 million, but the actual household registration in the concession is surveyed every five years. Each time a survey is conducted, there is no organization, lack of technology, and the actual population number is greatly missed. Therefore, the population of the city should be estimated at least at 5 million or more. Among a metropolis of 5 million people, how many people can hold real estate and houses? Let's assume that 10,000 people directly hold real estate houses, and 40,000 people indirectly hold real estate mortgage rights or real estate shares. The remaining 4.95 million people are tenants who pay rent every month. If the city's house prices rise sharply, the beneficiaries are 50,000 people, and the victims are 4.95 million people. If house prices fall, the clear beneficiaries are 4.95 million people, and the victims are 50,000 people. Should the government authorities and those responsible for social responsibility protect the interests of the smallest number of people and exploit more than 99% of the public, or should they take into account the interests of the largest number of people, so that they can coexist and prosper with the smallest number of landlords? This is the premise for discussing rent prices and should not be ignored. (To be continued)

Unidentified Man Dies of Illness on the Roadside 146

At the intersection of Xiexu Road and Luban Road in Western Shanghai, an unidentified man, approximately 30 years old, suddenly collapsed and died while passing by there yesterday morning. The Second District Police Bureau immediately ordered the guarantor Gu Xueyuan to report to the District Court to request an autopsy. Joint Meeting of the Rent Reduction Association in the South District the Day Before Yesterday 147

The Shanghai Nanshi District Rent Reduction Committee held a joint meeting of executive committee members of all district branches in the assembly hall of the association on Minguo Road the day before yesterday. Representatives from eighty-odd branches including the First Special District Sima Road and Second Special District Chongde Fang were in attendance. Yan Zhen was elected as chairman, and Ni Yi as secretary. After performing the ceremony, the following resolutions were passed: (1) Regarding the case of the landlord of Qingyun Lane, Zhizaoyu Road, cutting off the water supply without reason and falsely claiming rent arrears to the court for eviction, what measures should be taken? It was resolved that evidence of the impact of the water cut-off should be collected, and in addition to submitting a request to the party and government authorities, a lawsuit should be filed with the court to claim damages for the loss. As for the rent arrears, if a storage bank passbook is presented, the association is responsible for guaranteeing it. (2) Regarding the case of all tenants of Baoren Lane, Guohuo Road, suing the landlord in the District Court, the defendant in the first instance was not present, and there has been no further summons for two months, what should be done? It was resolved that a petition should be submitted to urge the summons. (3) The rent reduction dispute in Chengzhi Lane has been going on for four months. The landlord falsely filed a lawsuit. The court's judge was fully aware of the business difficulties and reduced the rent by four yuan per month, which has been resolved. It was resolved that the case be filed for record. (4) Rent reduction in Nanjing and Anqing has long been resolved, and the Hangzhou Municipal Government has decided that from September, rent will be paid at 70% of the original amount across the city. The situation in Shanghai's Nanshi, Zhabei, and Pudong is the same as that in the interior, and has been greatly affected by the (September 18th Incident) and (January 28th Incident), which is greater than in the interior. The rent reduction measures should be the same as in the interior at a minimum. If the landlord refuses to accept it, what should be done? It was resolved that the rent be deposited in a bank. (5) Landlords rely on the law and repeatedly initiate lawsuits. Tenants have tolerated it repeatedly to maintain relations, but the courthouse is as crowded as a marketplace, and business is as deserted as a bird's nest. Prolonged disputes are not a long-term solution. What should be done properly? It was resolved that all merchants and residents in the district should file a lawsuit with the court based on Article 74 of the Civil Code and Article 442 of the same law, demanding that landlords across the district reduce rents. The amount of rent and the year of construction will be the responsibility of each branch. If there is no branch, they may join the association. (6) All tenants in Sanduo Lane, Fangxie Road, have been forced to move by the landlord and request the association's assistance. It was resolved that a letter should be sent to the landlord first to withdraw the order. If the landlord refuses, more forceful measures will be taken. (7) The association published the Shanghai Rent Reduction Special Issue and submitted it to the Municipal Government for transfer to the Ministry of the Interior, and the Municipal Party Department for transfer to the Central Propaganda Department. Although enthusiasts have subsidized it by a dime per month, more than 150,000 copies have been distributed, and the fee is less than 5%. Because the fee is not generally collected, there are occasional criticisms, and the funding is insufficient. What should be done? It was resolved that publication should continue, and the expenses should be borne by the committee members. From the fifth issue onwards, distribution will be measured. If businesses and residents want to read the special issue, they must subscribe in advance. (8) The Bifang Lane branch has resolved the rent reduction since joining the association, and it has promised to contribute to the district (for the benefit of society). How should it be expressed? It was resolved that the association strives to solve the problems of the masses with the pain of our own body. Although the sincerity is commendable, it is inevitable that there will be outside criticism. It is hoped that the branches will not do this again in the future.

It was resolved that the first membership meeting would be held on October 14. The location would be announced after contact and confirmation. (B) Membership should be solicited by sending letters to team leaders and basic members. (C) Declarations should be distributed. (D) Wang Liansheng, Miao Lansheng, Li Mo, Shi Guoshan, Zhai Shiji, Feng Chengxin, Zhou Yushu, Tang Shaoming, Chen Zhisun, Chen Taigeng, Yang Canlin should be appointed to assist the team leaders and basic members in soliciting membership. The methods will be determined by Wang Liansheng. (3) Should a committee be established first to raise funds for the construction of the association hall? It was resolved that Li Mo, Gong Yuting, and Feng Chengxin should be appointed to draft the committee's organization and fundraising regulations and submit them to the general meeting for resolution. The meeting adjourned at approximately 5 pm.

Demolition Dispute in Sanduo Lane, Fangxie Road, Ximen 149

All Tenants in the Lane Hold an Emergency Meeting

The houses in Sanduo Lane, Fangxie Road, Ximen, Nanshi, belong to the Lan Guangyu Hall industry. They were rebuilt not long ago and are still strong and large. Unexpectedly, the landlord suddenly sent a large number of workers to build bamboo fences at 1 pm the day before yesterday, claiming that they must be rebuilt immediately and ordered the tenants to leave the houses. The tenants in the entire lane panicked and argued with the workers, pushing down all the bamboo fences, almost leading to violence. That night, all tenants in the lane held an emergency meeting. More than twenty households, including Zhu Ronglin, Ma Zengshou, Chen Shufu, Wei Songqing, Chen Yingzhou, Grandma Bao, Fan Qande, and Mao Chuntang, attended. Wei Songqing was elected as chairman, and he gave a report (omitted). Discussion: (1) It was agreed that the landlord's demolition was due to the failure to increase the rent. Using the excuse of rebuilding, without prior notice or seeking consent, and ordering the tenants to leave the houses, was illegal. What should be done? It was resolved that: A. The facts and circumstances should be reported to the party and government authorities, requesting assistance and upholding justice. B. Before the case is resolved, the rent due should be deposited in a bank for safekeeping. (2) How should the procedures for establishing the Sanduo Lane, Fangxie Road branch be carried out? It was resolved that a request should be submitted to the Shanghai Rent Reduction Association, South District, for record. (3) Appointment of duties. It was resolved that Wei Songqing, Chen Dufu, Fan Qande, Ma Zengshou, and Chen Yingzhou should be appointed as five comrades to be responsible for handling the matter. The meeting adjourned at 1 am.

Reading and Answering Questions

Attitude towards Occupation (Continued) 154

丨丨 Answer to Mr. Yuan Qingyan

The previous day, this article was suspended for one day because the (Reading News) was suspended. In the past two days, the main points of Mr. Yuan's letter have been extracted, and the general common problems of young people in this matter have been generally discussed. Today, I will focus on the attitude towards occupation to explain the reason for Mr. Yuan's worries. (Editor)

The root cause of Mr. Yuan's incorrect attitude towards occupation is nothing more than a problem belonging to the aspect of the attitude of young people towards life, which has already been discussed above. In principle, the above remarks can be said to have been answered. However, I still want to talk about it in more detail. Mr. Yuan used to plan to find his own way out in the rice business. This cannot be said to be wrong in terms of Mr. Yuan's actual life. However, Mr. Yuan cannot regard the rice business as an isolated thing that has no connection with everything else in society. If you just close your eyes and don't look at society and think that you can find all your hopes in the rice business, that is a big mistake. You must know that the rice business is only the smallest part of the entire society, like a small screw needle on a clock (this analogy is of course not very accurate, because the rice business has not the same relationship to society as a screw needle to the clock). It is responsible for circulating a bit of supply and is needed in today's social structure. However, it is impossible to estimate its survival and development separately. It will be affected by thousands of other social relations. If you close your eyes and want to find a way out in the rice business, the result will disappoint you sooner or later. When you see this, you may ask me, what kind of occupation in the world is fixed and can be completely unaffected by society? I replied! My friend, there is no such occupation in the world. In today's society, a change in one place will affect the whole. Who can be sure that their hopes will count? Here, I have told you, don't complain about your job, any other noble occupation is no different. Maybe you will ask me further, in this way, since everything we individuals rely on is an iceberg, what hope and way out is there in life? Then it is better to just get by. My friend, if you ask such a question, then I have to point out that this is wrong. This is your wrong view. You shouldn't just focus on the immediate interests of the individual. I have already said that it is impossible to find a way out starting from one person alone. You may have food to eat for the time being, or even a little extra, but if everyone around you has no food to eat, you cannot eat peacefully alone. People always want to survive! If there is no way to go, who doesn't want to find a way out? But to find a way out, don't go around in circles in an alley. You also need to find out which road this alley leads to, and how this road is connected to other roads. As for waiting to starve to death because you can't find a way out in the alley or because you failed to find one, that's only what the fewest people who have no life will do. There is always a way out in life! You have to put individual problems in the masses to solve. In an era when the masses cannot survive, naturally individuals cannot survive either. Then we should not plan too high for individual advantages and disadvantages, but pay attention to the interests of everyone that are the premise of my own survival. For example, when the Chinese nation is facing a serious crisis, we should focus our attention on the life and death of this great crisis. As for individual life? Naturally, we cannot ignore it, but we should not ignore society, and individuals should not demand too good a life or too fantastic a life. In this era, everyone should learn to endure hardships and live on solid ground, and should no longer sleep in the drum and daydream. As for occupation? We believe that as long as there is a little understanding of the purpose of struggle for individual life, any occupation is possible, and there is nothing noble or lowly. Our attitude towards occupation is to maintain the minimum level of existence. We should not have too high hopes for occupation, and at the same time, we will not have unbearable disappointments. Our social relations send me to the rice business, working as a street runner and river porter is of course very possible, even if my social relations are not so (noble), and can only let me work as a coolie, fill tea, pull a rickshaw, sell newspapers, or scrub people in a bathhouse, etc., what can't be done? It is all about seeking survival. People sing a certain song in a certain place and in a certain situation. As long as you still want to be a human being and have a certain goal, although occupations have high and low status, why insult myself? Why hate it. Of course, if you fantasize about being the chairman of the National Government when you are bored, that is not necessary. Because that is a harmful fantasy, not only can it not be realized, but it is also contrary to the overall social purpose by 18,000 miles.

Special Article

My Doubts Regarding Governor Clementi's Speech at the Malayan Association in London by Zhou Qigang (Continued) 156

Regarding the fourth point, "Placing all Chinese schools under Party control," I am a returned overseas Chinese and a member of the Chinese Nationalist Party. Regarding overseas Party affairs and overseas Chinese affairs, in spirit and duty, I feel deeply ashamed about this statement. According to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission's investigation last year, there are over 1,900 overseas Chinese schools. Fewer than ten are complete secondary schools; the rest are primary schools. Of these 1,900-plus schools, only about 110 have been registered with our Nationalist Government over the years. Despite the government's encouragement, over several years, less than 10% of these schools have a direct connection with the motherland. It's not just my personal disappointment; everyone involved in overseas Chinese education finds it strange. Because a country and its overseas citizens having a close cultural and educational relationship is natural, not exceptional. Our government is not even capable of making this obvious effort. Mr. Clementi insists that the Chinese Nationalist Party is placing all Chinese schools under Party control. We believe this is not malicious propaganda, but excessive flattery, making us feel so ashamed we want to disappear. Furthermore, 99.9% of overseas Chinese schools are primary schools. As mentioned above, the government's relationship with these schools is not close, and the students are young and lack knowledge. How can we talk about Party control? England is a leader in education. Even there, primary school students are not qualified to discuss politics. How much less so with the level of overseas Chinese students? The intelligent British government should be aware of this. Even Mr. Clementi, known as an "expert on China," probably laughs at himself for being overly concerned. As for how overseas Chinese education should be promoted and improved so that overseas Chinese students can achieve balanced development of their knowledge and maintain coexistence with other ethnic groups in their places of residence, this is originally worthy of the common attention of both Chinese and British people, but it is not appropriate to discuss it in this article.

Regarding the fifth point, "Compiling textbooks to instill anti-British thought," the words are consistent, but the events are different. Mr. Clementi used this as one of the reasons for dissolving the Malayan Chinese Nationalist Party. Therefore, "compiling" naturally refers to the Nationalist Party compiling. May I ask what textbooks the Nationalist Party has compiled? What are the titles of the books? On which pages does the anti-British thought appear? Books are evidence; they cannot be falsely accused. As far as we know (and the British government also knows), not only has the Malayan Chinese Nationalist Party not "compiled textbooks," but even the Chinese Nationalist Government's Ministry of Education has not "compiled textbooks." If there is any "compilation," it is by commercial publishers such as the Chung Hwa Book Company and the Commercial Press. It is definitely not compiled by the Malayan Chinese Nationalist Party. Mr. Clementi has the power as governor to dissolve the Nationalist Party; he should not exaggerate the facts to intimidate the British government. These textbooks compiled by merchants are mostly for business purposes. They are displayed in bookstores and people can choose what to buy. Readers have the freedom to choose. Furthermore, Mr. Clementi, as the head of Malaya, has already exercised his power to ban them. Why then use this as an excuse to dissolve the Malayan Chinese Nationalist Party? We believe Mr. Clementi has misspoke. Recalling last year, the Chung Hwa Book Company in Singapore, in order to adapt to the needs of the environment, specially invited Dr. Luo Liangzhu to edit various primary school textbooks. These were approved by the local Director of Education and ordered to be adopted by Chinese schools in various places. If such carefulness cannot avoid suspicion, it is not only a grave accusation against overseas Chinese but also implicates the local Director of Education. May I ask if Mr. Clementi would tolerate having a Director of Education under him with anti-British thoughts? (To be continued)

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 157

— (Yan Xinquan)

The young mistress got up especially early today to send a relative off on a ship. She got up at nine o'clock, and her whole day's demeanor was consequently listless. In the evening, she told the young master, "I slept two or three hours less this morning, and I felt unwell all day. The ancients said, 'The planning for the day lies in the morning!' How true those words are!"

Fishing Season 158

— Huang Kewei

September has arrived; in my hometown, September is the fishing season.

On the river, swollen with the autumn tide, those newly painted fishing boats, just dragged from the shipyard, floated like yellow leaves. On the night of the full moon in the fifteenth day, the fishermen would buy big fish and meat and piously worship the river god, so that he would protect them on their voyage. That night, they would heartily eat a meal of family reunion wine, then excitedly return to the boats, raise a small white sail, and leave their wives and children, braving danger to fight against the fierce winds and waves for a livelihood!

The women stood on the riverbank, watching the little seagull-like fishing boats drift downstream. A feeling of fear and hope weighed on their hearts. They murmured blessings for calm winds and tranquil waves ahead. They fervently hoped for a large catch of fish and a safe return.

If the merciless heavens sent violent storms and heavy rain, then they would hysterically cry out, disregarding the cold, disregarding the rain, running to the riverbank like madmen, watching the vast, turbulent river and wailing, or kneeling in the rain, praying to the heavens. How pitiful they are!

In recent years, boat rentals are high, taxes are numerous, fish prices are low, and the encroachment of foreign ships has added to the difficulty of fishing! Fishermen are forever struggling with hunger and death, but who among those who savor the fish knows how much of the fishermen's blood and sweat is mixed into this delicious taste?

September 18th and the Mid-Autumn Festival 159

— A Teacher in Retirement

Since the September 18th Incident left a huge mark of shame, up to today's September 18th, I fear the masses have faintly forgotten it, and only remember "The bright moon on August 15th"!

Thinking about September 18th in the past, we only shouted slogans, posted posters, and wrote propaganda articles. In the end, we left behind a commemorative day for raising flags and holding ceremonies, just for decoration.

Isn't the decoration of the Mid-Autumn Festival right before our eyes? Tall, beautiful incense towers, piled like pagodas; layers of delicious mooncakes, stacked like mountains; and all the other associated expenses. Which family doesn't spend money to prepare for the grand Mid-Autumn Festival? Who bothers with the nonsense of September 18th!

In the hall for commemorating the day of shame of September 18th, the adults and gentlemen, as usual, give speeches, with extremely mournful words. Someone said that after his speech, he might ask his wife to buy incense towers and mooncakes to decorate the Mid-Autumn Festival.

The masses all clapped their hands in unison. Amidst the applause, they dispersed in a crowd, busy buying incense towers and mooncakes, having long ago lightly tossed September 18th to the back of their minds.

There's a saying: "The toad insults the osprey; what is said is said, what is heard is heard." I ask, what do you think of this analogy?

Shadow of Xiangshan Pagoda 160

— Zhang Bingyuan

Xiangshan County in Guangdong Province, also known as "Iron City," is a famous and large county in the province, with the reputation of "lying down and earning 100,000" in the Qing Dynasty. This means that whoever governs this county does not need to work hard to accumulate wealth, and can safely lie down and earn 100,000 taels of silver annually. It is truly a coveted position. In the 17th year of the Republic (1928), the revolutionary government established its capital in Nanjing. Because this county is the hometown of Sun Yat-sen, it was specially renamed "Zhongshan County" and planned as a model county for the whole country, to show respect and commemorate him! Outside the west city of the county, there is a port called "Shiqi," which has been developed for decades. Chinese and foreigners live together, with countless sails and masts standing like a forest. It is a hub connecting the provinces, Hong Kong, and Macau, and ships can reach it directly in eight hours, making transportation extremely convenient. This is also the biggest reason for the prosperity of the county. From the west city district to the port, there is a thoroughfare called "West Gate Street," where shops line up densely and the essence of commerce gathers. However, although this city gate is set up, it is usually closed, and pedestrians must go around through the north and south gates. People are used to this and do not find it strange, nor do they find it a hardship to rush around. According to the old custom, it is only opened once on the eve of the Lunar New Year and on the morning of New Year's Day. The idea is that the end of the year and the beginning of the year are the days of cyclical renewal, and opening it once during this period can represent that it has not been closed during the year. How ridiculous the trends of the world are!

When it is about to be opened, the county magistrate informs everyone, acting quite solemnly. The restrictions are also extremely strict. If the gatekeeper accidentally opens or closes the gate at the wrong time, it is immediately recorded in the register. This shows the authority of the feudal system and is also due to superstition. On the riverbank opposite the west gate, there is a towering pagoda on Shanggang Hill, which was first built in the Tang Dynasty. Foreigners coming to China for trade all landed in Xiangshan County. This pagoda was used to observe the wind direction for navigation. It has a total of seventeen levels, directly facing the west gate. Every day at Wei time (1-3 pm), when the sun begins to decline, the shadow of the pagoda is reflected by the sunlight and falls into the circle of the city gate. This miracle only occurs in cloudy weather, when the sunlight is dim and the shadow is faintly visible. If the sun is blazing and there are no clouds, it cannot be seen. The construction is so strange that it seems to be the work of divine craftsmanship! Judging by scientific principles, there must be a great invention, but unfortunately no one has studied it. Because of occasional instances of unruly behavior by the people, it is blamed on the reflection of the pagoda shadow into the city gate circle. Over the generations, this explanation has been insisted upon, and so officials and people work together to tightly close the west gate to block the pagoda shadow. For hundreds of years, there has been no criticism, and the elders especially enjoy talking about it. When I left my hometown at the age of nine, when I said goodbye to the pagoda, I still saw the west gate tightly closed, as if deeply worried about the shadow's intrusion. Now that the county is called a model, and all affairs of state are flourishing, the city no longer exists. What the pagoda looks like, I cannot know. Perhaps after the changes of time, if the pagoda has a spirit, it will also follow the revolution and first revolutionize its heart, and now promote social customs of honesty and kindness?

Records of Fragrant Incense飘渺 161

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Except for his angry expression, Guangxu did not say anything or move his limbs. He clearly held the traitor who sold his freedom in utter contempt. His excessive coldness clearly told everyone that even though his one and only person—Yuan Shikai—was kneeling before him, he acted as if he did not see him.

Yuan Shikai was not unaware of the expression on Guangxu's face, but he already knew that this pitiful character could no longer take any action, so he paid absolutely no attention and remained very calm. After greeting the Empress Dowager, he casually said a few words. At the same time, the band, which was meant to be part of the grand welcoming ceremony, began to play. The band that Yuan Shikai had prepared was not ancient Chinese music, but a very pure Western band. There were probably twenty people, using the same instruments as a brass band in a foreign army. It is said that the bandleader was a student whom Yuan Shikai had paid to study music and composition in Germany. His technique was indeed very good. Especially at that time, he could truly be said to be one of the best Western musicians in China. After returning to China, he spent all his time teaching the young military officers whom Yuan Shikai had personally selected how to play Western music. It must have taken quite some time, because I heard them play very well!

Because Yuan Shikai himself was of military background, he deliberately made the various ceremonies for welcoming the Empress Dowager as military as possible. In addition to this band composed of twenty young military officers, he also brought in a large contingent of troops, all wearing helmets and armor, neatly arranged about a hundred yards from the platform, bowing to the Empress Dowager from afar. I really don't know why Yuan Shikai wanted them to do this. (131)

Ginkgo 162

— Zhen

Summer quietly left, and autumn, autumn, sure enough, arrived slowly.

Fried ginkgo is soft and glutinous, come quickly to count the ginkgo to eat! Three cents for one, six cents for two, nine cents for three. If the flavor is not good, don't pay!

This familiar song coming from the mouth of the fried ginkgo seller, again riding the breeze from the street into my ear canal, alas! It's that time of year again! I couldn't help but hum sadly. At the same time, a memory flashed through my mind like a movie: it was this time last year, whenever this wonderful song floated in the air, my eight-year-old younger brother would clamor, "Buy, Mom, buy!" Mom would put down her needlework and instruct the nanny. And in an instant, I would see the nanny running in from outside with a small basket full of ginkgo in the crook of her arm. At that time, my little brother's eyes would smile into slits, his mouth would open as wide as a dipper, he would jump up and down, and his little hands would grab wildly in the basket.

Time has passed imperceptibly. And now, summer has quietly left, and autumn has returned to the world. That light, wonderful song is again blowing in the breeze. But, heavens! Where is my mother now? Where is my little brother? The changes in human affairs are truly so unpredictable! Last winter, my mother and little brother both contracted incurable diseases and left my father and me for another world. And now, although the song still wafts as it did in the past, who will I hear clamoring for Mom again? Where can I find Mom again?

A wave of intense sadness gnaws at my stomach. At this time, the song faintly rose again: "Fried ginkgo is soft and glutinous,..." I couldn't help but immediately cover my ears with my hands, I couldn't bear to listen anymore.

Chatter

On Chinese Typesetting Fonts (Part 2) 164

— Zhang Zhenlu

The Commercial Press followed closely, producing typefaces similar to the Song dynasty font, the main differences being in the variations at the beginning of strokes, and the reduced slant of horizontal strokes. They called it "Antique Type".

The Commercial Press also produced a True Script (Zhenshu, that is, regular script) typeface, which when printed, looks roughly like handwritten regular script. Although it tends to appear a little stiff.

However, the range of sizes for this typeface was too small (usually six sizes are needed, from the largest to the sixth), insufficient for practical use, and there were many missing characters. Common characters were not cast. Whenever a hundred-character text was set, it was often necessary to specially engrave a few characters of this style to fill in the gaps, and the engraved characters could not be harmonized and integrated with the cast type; a few engraved characters spoiled the overall aesthetic, a truly regrettable thing! A foreign firm called the Commercial Printing House also cast True Script type, suffering from similar problems to the above. But I have seen countless intellectuals in China, countless people advocating industrial development to save the nation, thousands of stores and tens of thousands of factories across the country engaged in the printing business in Shanghai, and rarely anyone is interested in doing this work of innovating Chinese typefaces. But some foreign merchants took the lead, doing it for us. I fear that the study of inscriptions and seals will also have no one to study in our country, and foreigners will go ahead with it. That day is right before us!

Speaking of inscriptions, six or seven years ago, there was Yi Dachang, a master of inscriptions, skilled in writing, and adept at Six Dynasties script. He established the Huanan Publishing House on Wangping Street, preparing to produce a Wei stele-style typeface, making a great contribution to the future of culture. He painstakingly, over many years, according to the number of characters sequentially listed in the typeface case, wrote the Wei stele-style characters, five sets from large size to size five (that is, five different sizes of characters). He entrusted a foundry to make copper molds and cast the type. After a long time, only a few Wei stele-style type were cast. I have seen small items such as name cards printed with that typeface, and they were truly beautiful and pleasing, surpassing the various styles of other products. This was mostly because the calligraphy was both good and neat. Unfortunately, the foundry was too slow in completing the work, with no prospect of completion in sight. The Huanan Publishing House could not wait long and later closed down. This undertaking, which was so important to the future of our country's industry and artistic glory, was thus lightly extinguished. Perhaps not many people know about this matter, but even today, people still feel sorry for it when it is mentioned!

The revolution of Chinese typefaces is as described above. The Wei stele-style typeface created by Mr. Yi is even more like a martyr who sacrificed blood and life. These things have aroused the attention and sympathy of society. Therefore, there are now companies casting and selling True Script typefaces, which are manufactured more completely than those mentioned above. Especially in the last year or two, many more stores have opened to cast and sell imitation Song dynasty typefaces. Typefaces in the imitation Song dynasty style have become increasingly popular, almost usurping the position of the old Song dynasty style. Look, in recent printed products, not to mention the single-sheet parts used for commercial and personnel applications, even those so-called cultural vanguard subscription books, periodicals, small newspapers, etc., all follow the convenience of their environment and try their best to use typefaces other than the old Song dynasty style, in order to suit the tastes of readers and increase the aesthetic value of their publications. In short, this change and proliferation of typefaces is a good thing, but whether a typeface is good or not, whether it is superior or not, is another matter. Whether the craftsmanship of the new typeface is successful or not is yet another matter. These should be distinguished and dealt with by printing craftsmen and the public. If a typeface is not good and is truly unacceptable, it should be discarded by all. If a typeface is good but is made too badly, it should be guided and urged to reform. Only then can Chinese typefaces evolve and reach the realm of art. If you don't believe me, just look at the imitation Song dynasty typefaces that were poorly copied before there were cast and sold. If you were to gather them together to set and print a document, what kind of feeling would you get from this so-called imitation Song dynasty typeface? As for me, even when I see items printed with the so-called imitation Song dynasty typefaces that are now being cast and sold, if they are fundamentally flawed in the typeface model (even in the writing), I deeply lament that such crude workmanship is a disgrace to the country!
