Sports News

International Football Association Officially Announces Three Changes to the Rules of Football 165

The Sports Advancement Association Releases Translation

Decided to Implement and Apply from This Year

The National Sports Advancement Association has received the official announcement from the International Football Association regarding three changes to the rules of football and has decided to implement and apply them from this year. It is hoped that all regions will pay attention. The translation is as follows:

(1) Clause 1 of Chapter 5, fourth sentence, is merely a correction of English wording and does not change the meaning of the text. The originally used Chinese translation is already consistent with the meaning of the change, namely: "The player throwing the ball shall not touch the ball again before another player has touched it."

(2) Clause 1 of Chapter 10, sixth sentence, the old rule: "After being replaced, the player should enter the field when the game is stopped, report to the referee again, and only after being qualified can they rejoin the game."

New rule: "A player who has left the field due to the above example or for other reasons, or a player who has arrived after the game has already started, should re-enter or join the game when the game is paused and must report to the referee."

For violations of this rule, the referee should have the following judgment (this is a refereeing law, not a rule, so it is not recorded in the rule book): "A player who re-enters or arrives late and does not report to the referee should be warned. If the player commits other rules, they should be punished according to the rules."

(3) Explanation of Chapter 13 (also not the text of the rules)

"If the game is stopped due to a player's improper behavior, regardless of whether the player is only warned or is sent off, the opposing team should be given a free kick to continue the game."

Swimming Competition: Guangdong vs. Western YMCA 166

丨Twenty-five to Thirty-five Points丨

Liu Baoxi Sets New Western YMCA Record

100-Yard Backstroke in One Minute, Fourteen and Four-Tenths Seconds

The Shanghai and Guangdong swimming teams, with the temporary participation of four outstanding Chinese swimmers from the Hong Kong Interport Team, held a swimming competition last night against the Western YMCA. The audience was quite large. As a result of the competition, Guangdong unfortunately lost to the Western YMCA by a margin of twenty-five to thirty-five points. However, the competitive situation was extremely tense. The two outstanding athletes, Guo Zhenheng and Liu Baoxi, maintained their championships in breaststroke and backstroke respectively. Liu Baoxi even broke the Western YMCA's four-year-old 100-yard backstroke record with a time of one minute, fourteen and five-tenths seconds, which is truly remarkable and brings honor to the Chinese people.

New Backstroke Record. The backstroke competitors were Liu Baoxi and Jian Erming for Guangdong, and Kai Neng and Mai Liesto for the Western YMCA. Liu took the lead all the way, and the championship was never in doubt. He finished fifteen yards ahead of the second place finisher, with a time of one minute, fourteen and five and two-tenths seconds, breaking the previous Western YMCA record of one minute, fourteen and five and four-tenths seconds set in 1931. The Western YMCA record is held by a Chinese. Last autumn, Guo Zhenheng established a record of two minutes, forty-five and five-thirds seconds in the 200-yard breaststroke. Now Liu follows in Guo's footsteps, becoming the second person to do so. Last night, Jian Erming trailed Liu closely, ranking second. However, in the last twenty-five yards, he was overtaken by Mai Liesto due to lack of strength, finishing a hand's breadth behind in third place.

Breaststroke and Relay. Guo Zhenheng's first place in the 200-yard breaststroke was without question. However, there was an unexpected turn of events. Jian Erjie actually took the lead before Guo in the first eighty yards. The two Westerners lagged far behind. At eighty yards, Guo Zhenheng suddenly took the lead and won by a pool length to the finish, about twenty yards. Guo's time was two minutes, forty-five and five-thirds seconds, unfortunately short of his record of two minutes, forty-three and five-seconds set last year. The medley relay was easily won thanks to the efforts of the three major players, Guo, Liu, and Xu. However, in the 200-yard freestyle relay, they lost by an inch after fierce competition, which is a great pity.

Reasons for Defeat. The Guangdong team's defeat was due to the weakness in the two short-distance races and diving. The Western YMCA swept the top two places in the 50-yard race and diving. They only got second place in the 100-yard and 400-yard races. Therefore, even though they won in breaststroke and backstroke, it was ultimately to no avail. The results of the competition are as follows:

50-yard Freestyle: Glick (West), Smith (West), Zhou Ruiqin (Guangdong), 27 seconds.

100-yard Freestyle: Logan (West), Xu Heng (Guangdong), Staikowski (West), 61 seconds.

400-yard Freestyle: Logan (West), Xu Heng (Guangdong), Barrera (West), 5 minutes, 36 seconds.

100-yard Backstroke: Liu Baoxi (Guangdong), Mai Liesto (West), Jian Eryou (Guangdong), 1 minute, 14 seconds, 4 (New)

200-yard Breaststroke: Guo Zhenheng (Guangdong), Jian Erjie (Guangdong), Lan Gen (West), 2 minutes, 45 seconds, 6

Intermediate Hurdles Break North China Record

Women's and Other Performances Mediocre

(Jinan Correspondence) The provincial North China Preliminary Competition opened today (16th). The results for the whole day were mediocre, with no new records discovered. The men's advanced level, whether armed comrades, pistol brigades, or security teams, and especially the intermediate level, were in poor condition. Many did not meet the standard. The United States Has Not Yet Decided to Participate in the Olympics 170

German Sports Circles Express Hope

(Havas News Agency, Berlin, 17th) The Jewish people will be prohibited from participating in the 1936 Olympic Games held in Berlin. The United States has expressed opposition to this discrimination. The Chairman of the Olympic Committee of that country, Byron Tai Ji, recently said that he is not yet sure whether the United States will participate in the Games. German sports figures originally believed that the discriminatory measures against the Jews would not be implemented, so that the United States could join. Therefore, they were extremely disappointed to hear Bai's declaration.

Qiu Feihai's Letter Denies Initiating Meiyuan Gymnasium 172

The Talk of Being Director of the Tennis Department Is Groundless

Yesterday's newspaper reported that Qiu Feihai was one of the initiators of the Meiyuan Gymnasium and that he would be the director of the gymnasium's tennis department. Now we have received a letter from Mr. Qiu denying this. The original letter is attached below to clarify the truth (the above is omitted):

This morning I read your newspaper and saw in the sports news column that I and Mr. Scotten raised funds to build the Meiyuan Gymnasium and that I was appointed as the director of the gymnasium's tennis department. After reading it, I was very surprised. I have never met Mr. Scotten before, and I was not consulted beforehand about the establishment of the gymnasium. Only last month did Mr. Shi visit and consult with me, proposing that all competitions of the Shanghai Tennis Association, which I run, be held at the gymnasium during the season. It is still unclear whether this matter will proceed. Now it is suddenly said that I am the initiator of the association. I think it is a misunderstanding of the rumors. I am sending this letter to clarify and request that you correct it on my behalf. I would be very grateful. Qiu Feihai respectfully (September 18th)

[Educational News]

September 18th Commemoration 173

Dajiaolian's Sorrowful Declaration

Lost Territory Unrecovered, Great Hatred Unresolved

National Rights Unrevitalized, Resistance Unceasing

Yesterday was the third anniversary of September 18th. The United Association of Teachers and Staff of Shanghai Universities issued the following painful declaration: All compatriots across the country, please take note. What day is today? Is it not the day three years ago when the violent Japanese forcibly occupied our Shenyang, invaded our Northeast, burned and killed our people, and plundered our property? Is it not the most heartbreaking and shameful day that the violent Japanese trampled on our sovereignty and insulted our nation? Today, it has been three years. The white mountains and black waters have all fallen into a state of lawlessness. The north of the Great Wall and the south of the mouth are almost all colonial lands. Alas, compatriots, the Japanese imperialists are extremely vicious and ruthless, unprecedented. They take an inch and want a mile. They make endless demands. It seems that they will sweep across China, the map will change color, and the exploitation and oppression will be so severe that the people will have nothing left to eat. The blood of Goryeo still exists, and the ashes of Taiwan remain. Are our compatriots willing to sit idly by and be slaughtered by others? Alas, compatriots, the enemy is deep, the country is in danger. We should harbor the ambition to govern Wu early, like Goujian who slept on brushwood and tasted gall. We should quickly recover the hatred of the lost territory by recuperating and training. Farmers prepare food, workers make tools, merchants sell goods in the market, and soldiers and police deploy defenses in the field. All take that violent Japanese as our only great enemy and strive to resist humiliation. We colleagues in the academic and cultural circles should especially be determined to become strong, promote the theory of anti-Japanese resistance, instill the concept of anti-Japanese resistance, study specialized anti-Japanese academics, and practice the spirit of self-salvation in anti-Japanese resistance. We should work day and night, constantly thinking of this matter. Lost territory unrecovered, great hatred unresolved, national rights unrevitalized, resistance unceasing. The day our Chinese nation is completely independent will be the time for Sino-Japanese friendship and international peace. Alas, compatriots, the eight hundred followers of Tian Heng left their loyalty to the ages, and Shao Kang's one brigade left its glorious name to the ages. Although that violent Japanese is strong, what is there to fear? The wind and rain are as dark as night, but the rooster crows endlessly. We are willing to rise up with our compatriots across the country to plan for this.

The listeners were all moved, and the atmosphere in the entire auditorium was extremely tense.

Recent Situation of National Chiao Tung University 185

Mr. Li Zhaohuan, President of National Chiao Tung University, has recently been following the government's explicit instructions to raise standards and enrich content. Therefore, improvements in curriculum, equipment of mechanical instruments, addition of books, and expansion of various laboratories have been vigorously pursued, despite a reduction of more than 40,000 yuan in annual funding. A reporter recently interviewed officials of the university. The following is a record of the recent developments at the university.

(1) Graduated Students: The total number of graduates from the Shanghai main campus and the two colleges in Peiping and Tangshan was more than 230. In addition to more than ten students who have been admitted with government funding to study abroad through Jiangsu, Anhui, Henan, Northeast, Tsinghua, and the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee, about 20 others went abroad at their own expense. (This is the largest number of students studying abroad in the university's history.) As for the other graduates, in addition to those who had been pre-arranged for positions in construction organizations, banks, factories, and companies in various provinces and cities, the majority went to various railways in the country for internships. It is said that the initial trial results of the graduates from the two new departments of architecture and hydraulic engineering added in recent years to the Tangshan Engineering College, and the road engineering department added to the Shanghai main campus's Land and Civil Engineering College are all excellent.

(2) New Students This Year: In the two enrollment examinations for new students this year, there were more than 2,000 applicants from various regions. Because the university was ordered by the government to raise standards, the selection criteria were revised. Furthermore, the university has a fixed quota for each new student intake. Although there were qualified applicants in this year's enrollment, only a limited number were admitted due to the quota. Only 180 students were admitted to the various colleges of the Shanghai main campus, about 70 students were admitted to the civil engineering and mining and metallurgy departments of Tangshan, and about 35 students were admitted to the railway management department of Peiping. On average, one out of every seven applicants was admitted. The grades of each department were better than last year, indicating that the management of secondary schools in various regions has also improved. New students have now paid their fees and enrolled. The university held a welcome tea party for new students in the gymnasium the other day. The president, provost, deans of various colleges, dean of students, and dean of academic affairs all gave earnest speeches.

(3) Various Facilities: This year, the various colleges of the Shanghai main campus have seen considerable development. For example, the College of Management has added fourth-year classes in finance, railways, public affairs, and industry, and has also established a rolling stock laboratory, collecting various domestic and foreign rolling stock materials and statistics for students to practice. Furthermore, the College of Science has added a metallurgy department and newly established a special chemical laboratory, an optical electromagnetic laboratory, an industrial analysis laboratory, and an industrial chemistry laboratory, all of which have been fully equipped. The Tangshan metallurgy laboratory is under construction and is expected to be completed after autumn. As for the various engineering colleges, there are plans to add departments such as automotive engineering, aeronautical engineering, refrigeration engineering, textile engineering, electrical lighting engineering, and power communication. If funding is available, these departments can be established in sequence.

(4) Newly Hired Faculty: This year, most of the faculty members of the various colleges remain the same. Physics lecturer Mr. Mai Cunjian has taken leave to work as a mechanic on the Ping Sui Railway. Chemistry professor Dr. Shen Zhennan has taken a year's leave to go south to Guangxi Province to set up a sugar factory at the special invitation of the Guangxi Provincial Government. Transportation professor Dr. Zhou Fengtu has also taken a year's leave to handle joint transportation business at the special request of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. Due to the addition of various subjects in the College of Management and the College of Science, new professors have been hired, including Dr. Lin Die, former lecturer at New York University; Dr. Li Binghua, former professor at Yenching University; CPA Yu Xiji, former director of the Ministry of Finance; Dr. Xia Lai Lin, former president of Millard Academy; Gu Chengjun, former president of Peiping Women's College of Arts and Sciences; Tang Yan Yi, former director of the mathematics department of Jinan University; Dr. Ding Sixian, former dean of academic affairs of Anhui University, and other lecturers. Several new faculty members have also been hired at Tangshan College due to the addition of a fourth-year class in the mining and metallurgy department, such as Dr. Wang Junhao from the mining and metallurgy college of Columbia University, who is currently working in Shanghai.

(5) Rebuilding the Library Stacks: The university library has a large collection of Chinese and foreign books. The existing library building is insufficient, and the beams and columns are slightly skewed due to the heavy pressure of the books. For safety reasons, the addition of library stacks cannot be delayed. However, due to the high cost and limited university funds, it is impossible to cope. Former President Tang Wenzhi and others have launched a fundraising campaign among alumni and enthusiastic educators in various regions to remedy the situation. The reporter also interviewed a gentleman from the university's engineering department, who said that the buildings in the upper and middle courtyards are also quite dilapidated due to their age and must be rebuilt. However, since the private Nanyang Model Middle School occupies the south courtyard, even if minor repairs are made, there are no suitable buildings available for relocation, and the required expenses are very large and difficult to raise. University officials are deeply troubled by this.

Page 15

Free Talk

Dissent on "Creation and Time" 186

— Zhi Shui

(The completion of a great work requires a considerable amount of time. This is an undeniable fact in history.) Mr. Huang Huaibai told us this. He (casually cited a few examples), namely Goethe, Milton, and Byron.

History is accustomed to playing tricks on people. Mr. Huang cited examples that could prove his theory, but we can also cite examples to the contrary, right there in Mr. Huang's (history) book.

Starting from ancient times, the three tragedians of Greece cannot but be said to be great, right? Aeschylus lived to be sixty-nine years old (approximately) and wrote more than eighty tragedies; Sophocles lived to be ninety years old (approximately) and wrote about ninety tragedies (or perhaps one hundred and twenty-three); Euripides lived to be seventy-five years old and also wrote about a hundred plays. These three great tragedians cannot but be said to be (prolific), right? However, this did not prevent them from being (great).

But Greece is ultimately too ancient. Greek (history) is somewhat (mythical) and cannot be considered good evidence. We must cite more reliable (history). Then, Sir Walter Scott began writing novels in 1814 and, by 1829, with "Anne of Geierstein," he had written about 150,000 words of novels in twenty-one volumes over fifteen years. This can be said to be the first (prolific) record (in history), but the title of (great) did not escape from Sir Walter Scott. Alexandre Dumas's literary career began with the historical drama "Henry III" in February 1829. The novel "The Three Musketeers" was published in 1844, and the following year, the (sequel), "Twenty Years After," was published. Even if we say that Alexandre Dumas was preparing (historical novels) as early as 1839, then even including the time spent collecting materials, it would only be about five or six years before he wrote two (great works). Furthermore, looking at his (productive heyday), from 1842 to 1846, he completed two (trilogies) in just four years, and these two (trilogies) are precisely his most (great) works.

In addition, if we were to allocate time to Balzac, Tolstoy, or Zola, Mr. Huang Huaibai would feel that it was (too casual). However, Balzac and the others are still (great).

It can be seen that the issue of (creation and time) cannot be viewed rigidly. Even with the example cited by Mr. Huang Huaibai himself, Goethe's "Faust," Mr. Huang said that he (spent a full fifty years, from the age of twenty-three to eighty-three, to complete this masterpiece). However, in my opinion, these (fifty years) are worth studying. When we read Goethe's biography, we know that he was not exclusively working on "Faust" during those (fifty years). A writer may take many years from the initial idea of writing a book to its completion. Goethe is not the only one in (history) to have done so. However, we cannot rigidly say how many years it took to write that book.

Mr. Huang's advice to current writers not to produce shoddy work is correct. However, the basis of his argument is built on sand. If a writer does not have rich life experience, meticulous and sharp observation, and a systematic and mature way of thinking, then even if he (cherishes time) and spends ten years writing a sentence, it may not necessarily be a (great) work. Mr. Huang sets aside the writer's life experience and so on and only makes judgments based on the rigid relationship between (creation and time), citing Goethe and Milton as examples. This is difficult to convince current writers. Or is Mr. Huang's so-called (requiring a considerable amount of time) referring to the acquisition of rich life experience, the development of meticulous and sharp observation, and the maturation of thought? If so, then Mr. Huang's examples are not applicable. Judging from the examples cited by Mr. Huang and his criticisms of current writers, it must be said that his concept is limited to a rigid temporal relationship. ((The Eve of September 18th Incident))

Letter from the Countryside 187

— Xi

Again, the handwriting of a very withered hand, accustomed to holding a hoe

Holding a pen also brings out the flavor of the hoe.

× × ×

(Home is even worse than before), is that a sigh to the setting sun? Can an old person be like before?

× × ×

Every word is the voice of an old person,

× × ×

Driving the ox in the morning mist, so hoarse and deep, it should be even more hoarse and deep.

× × ×

Every word is the eyes of an old person, watching the threshing ground in front of the house all day long, what kind of hope is given to the young people?

On Mr. Mu Shiying's "(On Sorrow)" 188

— Wan Dihe

Mr. Mu Shiying said in Free Talk "(On Sorrow)":

(In our literature, sorrow is two words that are loved by people: and the emotion of sorrow is also very easily popular among young people. The lyrics of Li Houzhu, Li Qingzhao, and Nalan Chengde, and the poems of Li Yishan are sold in various versions in the market; some novels shrouded in cheap sentimentalism, such as "The Sorrows of Young Werther," "Downfall," "Lost Lamb," "Immensee," "La Dame aux Camélias," and even "A Smile in a Dream," which completely imitates "Immensee," are cherished by the broad masses; the tone of "Oh, sorrow" permeates the conversations and correspondence of young people; a gloomy face is regarded as the temperament of a poet; these are all readily available examples.)

However, his view is incorrect; such a thing once happened: an author, in a certain time and under certain circumstances, used sorrow and tears to complete his artwork; readers in a certain place would also regard this artwork as a precious treasure; however, when the time and place change, the author's emotions and the readers' tastes will be completely different; therefore, the (masses) who currently regard "Immensee" and the like as treasures, and the (young people) whose tone is filled with (Oh, sorrow), will probably be regarded as waste by another kind of young people and the masses.

Mr. Village Chief (5) 189

— Wang Renshu

From the drawer of the black and sour account table, a notice was taken out and unfolded to take a look. It was written like this:

(······

((1) The purpose of organizing reserve soldiers this time is to train your ability to defend yourselves, not to call you to join the army. You must all abide by the law and act accordingly.

((2) The training period for each term is stipulated to be two months. During this month, the county will subsidize food expenses. The cost of clothing and other expenses will also be provided by the county. After the expiration of the term, you will still be allowed to return to your villages.

((3) The total number of people in the first phase is 50, which will be drawn in proportion to the number of able-bodied men in each village.······

((4) ······

(In summary, you must all abide by the above provisions. Otherwise, severe punishment will be inflicted without pardon······)

Mr. Feng Wen recognized it for a while and handed it to Crippled Ke Sheng.

(What exactly does this say?) Crippled Ke Sheng still unfolded the notice without putting it away. (People in the village say that it is drawing conscripts. With this kind of drawing method, I am afraid that no one will go.)

(You are really a fool!) Mr. Feng Wen felt that he should lose his temper this time. (I have told you so many times, it is not drawing conscripts, it is training reserve soldiers! However, the age is limited to over 20 and under 40! Moreover, you will come back after two months of training!)

(Oh, oh!) Winter Sheng, who was not very patient originally, has now learned to be very amiable. (Are you going to learn to drill? Will you really be released after learning to drill for two months?)

(Of course! The county magistrate has told me personally, and the district chief has also told me personally, but you still won't rely on you.)

Mr. Feng Wen sat down on the bamboo chair with a thud. The bamboo chair made a gurgling sound as if it were suffering for someone else.

Third Anniversary (Part 2) 190

— Li Huiying

(Grandma. Mommy is asleep.)

Running over with a patter, while talking, Xiao Lan walked to her grandmother's side. The old woman Huang grabbed her good hand, wanting to ask her something, but suddenly felt something cool on her hand. Looking down, tears were flowing from the child's face. She couldn't help but panic and asked:

(Why are you crying, Xiao Lan?)

The child did not make a sound, but just shook her head.

(Did Mom hit you?)

(Mom didn't.)

(Then what's wrong with you?)

(I don't know what's wrong, I see Mom crying, and I cried too. Mom showed me Dad's picture, and I thought of Dad, and I couldn't stop crying.)

The old woman Huang comforted her granddaughter while pulling her hand to the outer room.

The daughter-in-law's room was dark, the light was turned off. The old woman Huang groped her way to the door and heard sobbing inside. The child shouted:

(Mom, Grandma is here.)

The old woman Huang felt a pang of heartache, and tears fell like rain. She grabbed the door frame with one hand, preventing herself from falling, and said tremblingly:

(Daughter-in-law, you, ······ you ······ you are crying?)

The daughter-in-law did not answer. She was lying on the kang, quietly moved her body, turned on the light, and got off the kang. A large area of the kang mat was stained with tears. Taking the child's hand, she said in a low voice:

(Grandma, sit for a while.)

After settling down, the old woman Huang asked:

(Tomorrow is the third anniversary, the third anniversary of Xiao Lan's father, but have you remembered it too? I was just about to tell you.)

(Alright, Grandma, don't think about these things, it's useless to think about them, you can't bring them back to life.)

(Are you comforting me? Why are you still crying?)

(I'm not like you.)

(I feel like I've suffered more pain than you. To tell you the truth: the eldest died, the second ran away, I have to live my life, and I'm always sad for you. Why is my life so bad, ······)

Speaking of this, the old woman Huang was filled with grief and could no longer continue her words. She just stared blankly at the small, bean-sized light. The daughter-in-law and child both focused their eyes on a photo of a man in military uniform.

The countryside on an autumn night is quiet and solemn. Encountering these turbulent times, no one travels at night, and even a few barks of dogs cannot evoke any associations. Only the chirping and chirping autumn insects call out, decorating this silent night, but in fact, it is better to say that they are lamenting the imminent end of life, singing sad songs for themselves. The strong scent of grain is released day and night, as if telling people that they have completed their mission. The dark sky covers the dark earth. This human world seems to be just struggling in the darkness.

The old woman Huang looked at the light, and suddenly a burst of dizziness in front of her eyes made her see a night in Changchun three years ago, the night her eldest son died. She saw how her son was beaten to death by Japanese soldiers, and many soldiers also lost their lives. Fire and shelling destroyed the entire barracks. She also saw her second son, who acted almost like a bandit, together with people carrying guns, calling themselves Red Beards, and shouting that they were the Volunteer Army, dedicated to fighting the Japanese soldiers and fighting them to the death······

The old woman Huang also remembered the situation of being bullied by the officials in the past three years: since the death of her eldest son, there were no servants in the family, and the police in the district no longer looked at her with such high regard as before. Every time taxes were apportioned, they would definitely apportion more than others. Also, the self-defense corps often came to demand people, demanding her second son, saying that he had joined a bandit gang and harmed the local area. Every time they came, they had to be tipped off more or less. These things, inside and outside, made the old woman Huang feel that the world was becoming too out of shape, and people's hearts were becoming too evil.

(Mom, will Dad really never come back?)

After being dazed for a while, Xiao Lan suddenly said a sentence. The old woman Huang blinked her eyes. She said with a sentimental and indignant tone:

(Xiao Lan, your dad was killed by Japanese soldiers, how can he come back? Alas! A pitiful death. But don't forget this, and take revenge for your dad in the future! Alas! Why did he die, was it his fate to die! Why doesn't fate help people!)

(I heard that many people died that time,) the daughter-in-law said, moving her eyes from the photo to her mother-in-law's face, (Grandma, you always believe in bad fate, but does that mean that all those who died had bad fate? I don't believe in such things!)

The old woman Huang could not answer her daughter-in-law's words. She had encountered this situation more than once, but this time she was still the same as before, not angry, nor showing any embarrassment. After a while, she changed the subject and said:

(Aren't we going to the grave tomorrow? Then, we need to fold paper ingots.)

Xiao Ju interjected and said:

(I want to fold gold ingots for Dad, fold a big, yellow gold ingot.)

(Burning paper and money, I don't really believe in these things, and I don't have the mood to do it. I just hope that someone can drive the Japanese soldiers out, and I'll fold paper ingots every day and burn incense every night. But it's the third anniversary, and in these three years, I haven't heard of many troops fighting the Japanese soldiers! Our people died in vain, and no one has been given a chance to avenge them.)

Although she said so, she still squatted down and took out the paper foil from the cabinet with her right hand.

Xiao Lan shouted again, as if very happy:

(I want to fold gold ingots for Dad, fold a big, yellow gold ingot.)

The old woman Huang saw her daughter-in-law crying again. She felt very sad, and reached out several times before she could grab two gold foils, finally, she also cried.

Gold and Foreign Exchange Pressures Lead to Another $2.20 Drop in Premium 191

Both New and Old Contracts Retreat Below $50

September Contracts Completely Liquidated

Yesterday, the gold market continued to weaken. Banks were eager to sell, resulting in numerous sellers in the market, pushing prices below the $50 threshold. The morning began with overseas silver markets showing a slight contraction in the UK and stability in the US. London spot gold rose by half a penny. Exchange rates were flat, US cotton rose by thirteen points, US wheat rose by one point, and stocks fell slightly. In off-market pre-trading, prices initially rose by over two dollars, but after a large transaction at the close, rumors of US buying activity emerged, and sellers became active, creating a very flat market. The opening saw a slight increase, but banks immediately put pressure on the market, hardening exchange rates and breaking through the $50 mark. However, due to prior knowledge that the HSBC exchange rates for both British and American currencies would remain unchanged, there were many buyers at the lower prices, leading to a rebound. At this point, the market struggled around the $50 level. Slightly negative rumors spread, and the banks' appetite for supply exceeded demand, leading to an oversupply in the domestic market, causing speculators to sell off. Another round of declines began, with active trading between banks and some opportunistic buying at cheaper prices. After the lows, the market entered a prolonged period of stagnation. Finally, as the foreign exchange market stabilized, scattered small investors showed some buying interest, but trading was limited, and the price briefly rose above $50. However, the ample supply then pushed it back below $50 by midday. The underlying trend remained stable, and the aftermarket opened steadily. Subsequently, the domestic market loosened again, and initial reports from Bombay indicated a rise of 1.2.2 annas followed by a decline. However, opportunistic buyers emerged, stabilizing sentiment. The gold market has entered a period of mediocrity. The December new standard also declined, but the overall day's trend remained relatively stable. Stagnation of Grain, Flour, and Wheat Intensifies 205

After the morning opening of the flour market, prices for all months showed a consistent trend of stagnation. Although the quoted price for foreign wheat in Chicago was better by two to three dimes and Canadian wheat by one to three dimes, there was little activity at the opening due to slow sales in the north. In the Jiangzhe hinterland, mooncakes were already losing popularity, making sales even more difficult. Additionally, concerns about warehouse rent affected some forward contracts, causing near and distant prices to gradually decline, dropping by about one cent from the previous day. By the afternoon opening, the current month saw some profit-taking by outside speculators, while factory orders remained sluggish, leading to a gradual decline. There was little interest from customers in distant contracts, and prices also softened. As actual sales showed no improvement, the trend remained sluggish. Ultimately, the current month fell by two cents, October by one cent and seven and a half mills, November by two cents and two and a half mills, December and January by one cent and seven and a half mills, and February by one cent and a half.

After the morning opening of the wheat market, prices for all months generally remained stable. Although the quoted price for foreign wheat in Chicago was better by two to three dimes and Canadian wheat by one to three dimes, buyer interest was not strong at the opening, and sellers were also scarce. This resulted in a stalemate with no significant price movement. By the afternoon opening, influenced by the weakness in the flour market and the nearing delivery date for the current month, outside speculators slightly reduced their positions, causing market sentiment to turn weak. Distant contracts also saw some profit-taking, and opening prices declined. However, trading was very thin, and these fluctuations were indeed minimal. Ultimately, the current month was down by two small cents, October by three cents, November by five cents, December by four cents, and January by five cents. Spot wheat saw factory demand stall, and no new business was being conducted.

Slight Rebound in Su Tonghou's Japonica Rice 206

(Shanghai South) The various "gangs" (merchant groups) arriving mainly consisted of those labeled as numbers twelve and thirteen (with a total of nearly two thousand shi [unit of volume]), and market sentiment was relatively positive. Due to a perceived tight supply situation, the price of various grades of japonica rice saw a slight rebound of about a "jiao" (one-tenth of a yuan). However, spot sales of late-season rice from various "gangs" felt notably sluggish. Reliance was solely on bulk purchases, with the Qingdao and Yantai gangs stepping in to buy over five hundred packages. Market conditions remained stable but with a slightly tight undercurrent. However, given the stop-and-start nature of the buyer "gangs," future trends remain difficult to predict. Approaching the holiday season, financial constraints are keenly felt, making it difficult to achieve a favorable market situation before the holidays. The arrival of new japonica rice is gradually increasing, but sales are stagnant, leading to a drop of over two "chi" (unit of length, here likely referring to price). However, various grades of new "jian" rice are able to maintain supply and demand parity, with little price volatility. The same goes for "bian yuan" rice. Factories are only offering a new price of ten yuan and eight "jiao."

(Shanghai North) Yesterday, the supply from various sources down the river (Jiangsu) were of the 14th and 15th grades. The market showed some improvement in clearing goods that were skillfully selected. The market price of white japonica rice was down by about one "jiao," and white "yuan" rice was down by nearly a "jiao." New "yang jian" rice was down by two "jiao," new and old "ke jian" rice was down by a few "fen" (one-hundredth of a yuan), western new japonica rice was down by more than a "chi," and eastern new japonica rice was down by two "jiao." Thin rice was scarce, with prices high and the market fatigued.

Revival of Sales of Zhangzhou Brown Rice 207

Yesterday, the market conditions for foreign customer's "xian" rice (long-grain rice) remained fair and stable. The production price of foreign rice rose slightly, with hoarders reluctant to sell. Buyers were generally not very interested in purchasing, and the market turned quiet. There was only one transaction of 200 tons of small returned goods from March, priced at five yuan, one "jiao" and six "fen," which was up five to six "fen" from the previous week. There were no other transactions. The spot market for foreign rice still has a large inventory, but everyone is waiting and watching. The total market volume was only 1,433 packages, with prices similar to the previous market, but the situation showed a slight improvement. Customer's "xian" rice was very dull, while brown rice was selling well in the hinterland of this street. The Zhangzhou rice, which had previously caused disputes, has been proven to be a product of southern Fujian. However, due to being detained for several days, the price repeatedly dropped. Yesterday, a hinterland street purchased 3,000 packages of brown rice, and the price rose by five "fen" to a "jiao." There are still over 8,000 packages in the market, and there is hope for sales to improve in the coming days. All other brown rice and other rice varieties totaled less than 1,000 packages, and the market was generally stable.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

Middle School Principal Flees with Funds 212

— Wen Bing

Shanghai has always been a world of scams, but such scams have not been very common in the education sector. The newspaper reported the other day that Shi Yunjin, from Haimen, Jiangsu, established the Dajiang Vocational Middle School at 1034 Tangshan Road in Shanghai during this year's summer vacation. Student recruitment and school affairs were managed by his father, Shi Tangmin, and brothers Shi Yunlong and Yuncheng. Shi, a graduate of a certain university, appointed himself as the principal and recruited over 130 students. Unexpectedly, the Shi family, father and sons, on August 31 (the day before classes were scheduled to begin), packed up all the school's assets and fled.

The 130-plus students were naturally thrown into a state of confusion, completely baffled and panicking. They then drafted a declaration appealing to all sectors of society. In addition to exposing the above-mentioned facts and realities, the declaration also included a poignant description of their plight, worth quoting a few sentences: ("...Tears are useless, and there is nowhere to turn. We are stranded in a state of being out of school. In this year of social and economic bankruptcy, it is already very difficult for our parents to send their children to middle school for education. Now, this unfortunate event is so heartbreaking..."). ("...Rather than saying it's a school fraud, it's more accurate to say it's a family's conspiracy. ...We request severe punishment for the Shi family, father and sons, who are social bandits, engaging in hooligan behavior and disgracing the education sector...").

This kind of educational scam is not entirely absent in this evil society of Shanghai. However, in the past, it seemed to be limited to those cram schools (whose sole purpose was to make a profit) or very small alleyway elementary schools. They would place an advertisement in the newspaper, collect a sum of money, and then abscond. The harm caused was limited to a small number of people.

But this time, the scale is much larger. I often hear people saying that Chinese education is bankrupt. The performance of this event has truly shocked the Chinese masses. A dignified middle school, a dignified bachelor-principal, are now serving as the vanguard of educational bankruptcy. Where is Chinese education headed? This is a question that should be raised.

Shanghai, Shanghai, was originally a "paradise," and Shanghai's education has always been regarded as "heavenly education." Young people in the interior all yearn to come to Shanghai! Elementary school students hope to come to Shanghai for middle school, and middle school students hope to come to Shanghai for university. Therefore, the outer shell of Shanghai's education has become very developed. Even though schools are as dense as shops, students still flock to them like a tide. This year, the entire country is mired in a severe drought and flood disaster, and schools in the interior are all feeling the loss of students, but Shanghai is still very prosperous.

However, Shanghai is ultimately like a paper tiger. The economic downturn in the city can be seen from the rows of businesses closing down on Avenue Edward VII, and one can imagine the situation elsewhere. Therefore, all kinds of scams are being staged even more fiercely.

This middle school principal's flight with funds is a powerful illustration of this.

Page 19

Night Record in Autumn Rain 213

— Bai She

Jingan Temple Road on a rainy night.

The neon lights cast many winding, beautiful reflections on the road surface, and the road, washed by the rain, is a shallow stream!

In recent years, my life has been too far removed from the city. In my mind, it seems that daytime has light, and nighttime is only fit for enduring in darkness. When a single candle is lit, facing the dimness of the four walls, I dare not generate any more hope. Life seems to have a rhythm, but it always feels too rigid.

Thinking back, it was early summer when I came to Shanghai from the water villages of the South. The city's high-speed energy gave me a lot of temptation, and I generated many illusions during my journey. Excitement was, of course, inevitable. But after arriving in Shanghai, life diverged sharply from my ideals. I really don't understand why ideals always fail to materialize. The scramble for food made it hard for me to catch my breath, and the high-speed everything accentuated my own slowness.

After a month in the countryside, I still longed for Shanghai. Often, gazing at the sky of Shanghai, reddened by lights, I over-praised Shanghai in my heart. But at this moment, strolling in the heart of this city, I am wooden and unresponsive. The rain is seeping in densely from the broken seams of the umbrella. Passing the Simmons billboard, the woman on the Simmons is also soaked, smiling lazily.

Turning the corner, the clock on the Racecourse pointed to seven o'clock. Looking further afield, isn't that Shanghai's night market? High on the rooftops of the big companies, red and blue lines are running. We should think of going into its embrace, of the coquettish eyes of the night tour, but the rain is getting heavier.

I walk in the torrential rain, I laugh, because I have no purpose and no hope. Rainy days show a special charm. Am I seeking a bitter poem?

The men and women immersed in the Silver Palace are now being spat out by that beautiful wide mouth. Before they have even finished savoring the plot, they are hit head-on by this sudden rain. Pleasure is so difficult and never lasts!

The raindrops are becoming denser and heavier, and the neon-red market, like a dream, is shrouded in a layer of dream-like gauze. The neon signs embedded in the deep blue sky are gradually blurring, blurring to the point of being unrecognizable. Yes, Shanghai is such a blurred, unrecognizable thing.

By the time I reached my lodgings, my clothes were already soaked through. Entering the room, a wave of damp, stuffy air rushed to my head. The sound of the rain was still intense. When the sky clears, autumn will be several degrees older. I was still thinking this as I went to sleep.

Endless Nonsense 214

— Wen Gai

Someone who has experienced hunger knows how hard hunger is. If you ask a well-fed person what hunger feels like, they can't even imagine it. Even if they can imagine it, it won't be very real.

Once upon a time, there was an emperor who heard his ministers report that "the people are starving and have no food to eat." He asked without hesitation, "Why don't you teach them to eat porridge?" Well-fed people assume that people who have no rice to eat don't eat porridge. In fact, people who can eat a meal of porridge a day are not in a bad situation. There are many more people in this world who can't even dream of eating a meal of porridge a day.

There was also the son of a wealthy family who was always full from eating snacks all day long. His mother still forced him to eat rice and porridge five times a day. He told people: "Eating is really torture!" Well-fed people are strangers to hunger, so they naturally hate eating.

Semonoy's novel "Hunger" depicts the physiological and psychological abnormalities of hungry people with exquisite detail. But if you've seen Chaplin's film "The Gold Rush," that kind of performance can move you even more. When a person is hungry, their physiology changes, and their eyes are blurred. He repeatedly mistook his companions for a big hen, and he wanted to eat the big hen, but when he looked closely, it was his companion. How profound a performance is that?

Hesitation 215

— Wei Nan

The sunset glow is gradually, gradually fading away. In the west, which is rendered in the golden glow of the setting sun, countless returning crows are flying in rows towards the vast end of the sky. Ah! At this evening hour, when everything needs a destination, isn't it the hard-working peasant women of the suburbs dragging their tired souls towards their destination, the home hiding in the woods over there?

Although here, one is spared the attacks of the city's troubles, the encirclement of those inherent sounds of the marketplace, but it is divorced from that sinful rendering. However, the sounds of the factories letting off steam at dusk and at dawn are truly difficult to escape the trampling of bad luck!

A crow sometimes cries out one or two sad sounds. In the rustling of the fallen leaves of this dusk, in the gentle, soft sway of the evening breeze, here it does not disturb this natural elegy. However, in my heart, it draws a shadow of sorrow. In the lonely soul of a wanderer fallen to the ends of the earth, a tragic exile in a foreign land who has lost his destination, hesitating so lost in this suburb of a city pregnant with misery. If hesitation did not require bread, then I would willingly hesitate like this. However, the need for the burning of hunger, the need for clothes, and the prayer for a destination... people cannot dream so much, can they?

The sky is gradually getting darker, and a dim magic veil is about to envelop the earth. However, how will I, this hesitating ghost, settle myself? In the woods over there? No. In this vast wilderness, who can guarantee that no wild beasts will come? At someone's house over there? Who is your friend, who is your relative? Moreover, in this vast and ruthless crowd, even friends and relatives are different in that they fawn over the rich. Although one says that these strangers might pity you, a beggar-like person? It's even less possible to go under those skyscrapers over there. There are too many unemployed and breadless wanderers! Hesitate, hesitate, in this long darkness, let him do a somersault!

Page 20

A Dark Heart 216

— Sha Fei

It's autumn!

Stepping on the fallen leaves of the plane trees, in the afterglow of dusk, I walked alone across that long embankment. When my small building, where I had lived for so many years, came into view, my footsteps slowed down as if being dragged backwards: a dark heart, a dark heart locked in that dark building!

Youth has been wasted like this, the long days of five years!

She took my hand and said softly, five years ago, to cherish my sister and my small building as if cherishing me? I contained my tears, like a lone goose lost in the autumn sky, leaving its sorrow in the world. She stopped her last breath.

So I and a twelve-year-old girl guarded this small building, like an old monk in meditation; forgetting the world, forgetting friends. Watching the peach blossoms bloom and fall from the window; listening to the angry roar of thunder in the middle of the night; the autumn wind bringing white snow flakes in bursts; I stared at the good-looking photo and asked the girl;

(It's another year?)

(It's another year! Brother-in-law, when will we leave here?)

A pair of black eyes, the same as in the photo, flashed in front of me (When the autumn geese return,)

The girl suddenly pulled my hand, left the small building, crossed the long embankment, and went to her grave.

The green grass on the ground was green and lovely again; the orioles returned, singing enchanting spring songs; the dust on the tombstone had been swept away by the willow branches; but why was the woman in the white dress crying so sadly?

I looked up for no reason, white clouds chasing white clouds, weaving a beautiful sky.

(Sister,) the girl said, holding the tombstone: (When the autumn geese return, we will leave here, don't you feel lonely, sister, I'll give you a bouquet of small flowers.)

She picked the wildflowers in front of the grave, put them on the stone steps, and stared down at the tips of her own shoes.

Sorrow, desolation, overwhelmed the girl's heart; but, but when the autumn geese returned, she could not stand the loneliness of the small building, left me, left her sister's grave, and left, with no news of her for a year.

It's autumn!

I supported myself with a cane, with a heavy heart, and with heavy steps, went alone to the graveyard. The tombstone had been eroded by wind and rain, and was no longer so smooth and glossy. The withered branches of the wildflowers had long been taken away by the autumn wind, like the withered yellow plane tree leaves; like that pair of big black eyes, before my eyes was desolation, loneliness, only the crying of the woman in white accompanied my endless sorrow.

Looking up, white clouds chasing white clouds, a picture of autumn's beautiful sky!

On the long embankment, gazing at that dark small building, five years!

Childhood Memories 217

— Rou Wu

Time passes ruthlessly, like flowing water. It's been ten years since my father and mother died.

My father was similar to most fathers, but more capable and strict than my mother. He didn't have the same enthusiasm for playing with the children as my mother did. He was struggling in life all day long. And my mother? Just the opposite of my father, she was kind and affectionate. She loved me as much as she loved her own life. When I returned from school every afternoon, she would put down whatever she was doing and hold me in her arms, kissing me passionately. Sometimes she would tell me to pout my little lips and gently tap them. Then she would call out a string of loving words: (My child! My good child! My darling, my precious!), as if she wanted to swallow me whole. However, my mother's love for me made me less close to her, and I often liked to be near my father, who didn't love me so much. But my father's love for me couldn't match even one-third of my mother's. Sometimes I would stand very close to him, hoping he would hug me for a moment, or touch me, or at least look at me, but it was impossible. He wore a pair of reading glasses, wrinkled his brow, and had a solemn face, holding a brush in one hand and manipulating abacus beads in the other. His face twitched as if he were muttering something. Sometimes he looked unhappy, and sometimes he showed a very happy face. He was just calculating his confounded accounts. When I couldn't get my father's love, I would take it out on my mother, falling into her arms, clenching my small fists, and hitting my mother's chest desperately, but my mother didn't stop me in any way, nor did she cry out in pain. Instead, she smiled and said to me: (Good darling, hit harder, hit harder.)

She seemed to enjoy being hit by me, and as a result, my hands became sore. I hadn't released my anger, but instead increased my anger. I had no choice but to hide in my mother's arms and cry inexplicably. This situation often caused my mother to suffer, not knowing why. At this time, she would be anxious and sweating, wrinkling her brow and saying: (Darling! Are you not feeling well anywhere? Do you want to buy something? Tell me! Mom will go to the street to buy it for you.)

When my mother said this, I cried even harder, even more vigorously. I didn't stop until I was extremely tired and fell asleep. Because of this, my mother sighed in pain all the time.

Thinking about such things now, there is only bewilderment, only tears falling uncontrollably! That stern father and kind mother passed away one after another ten years ago. One was cruelly beaten to death by bandits, and one died of illness within a short period of time. At the same time, I don't know where my childhood heart has gone. Alas! Everything from childhood is no longer attainable, the past is not to be recalled!

Page 21

Autumn Window Musings - Part Two 218

— Jun

Remembering Old Friends in the South

Autumn in the South is the delightful season when longans come to market.

That distant sea, that distant shore, deeply buries the golden dreams and golden yearnings of my youth. Everything there is charming: the sky is jade-like, all azure blue, and the sea is also azure, lying under the warm, tranquil sunshine, rippling with boundless, gentle waves. Every dusk, with a light heart, I would stroll with a woman through the dense shade of the longan trees, watching the sunset on the opposite shore reflected in the heart of the sea, faintly weaving into brilliant colorful clouds, listening to the tiny waves at our feet, gnawing at the beach with cricket-like sounds, sometimes receding, then soon washing back up again. It was like listening to the rhythms of natural music.

Intoxicated in that poetic dusk, shoulder to shoulder, whispering sweet nothings, time would just pass by like that, forgetting to return home, sitting on stone benches until the moon poured silver light from the gaps in the trees into the deep night…

Autumn has come again, ah, my golden dreams, and golden yearnings?

My body, I don’t know when, has drifted to this foreign land, while my soul still flies to that distant, distant other side of the sea. That side of the sea once held traces of my private affections, that side of the sea has already buried golden dreams, golden yearnings, perhaps even covered with a thick layer of mud and sand, a thick layer of the mud and sand of years.

The honeyed taste of longans and their black, bead-like seeds, ah!

Whenever I think of autumn in the South, I can’t help but think of Linlin, nourished in the warm sunshine, with those moving, black, longan-seed-like eyes, Linlin, who has a melodious, musical voice and black eyes and hair. And that clear smile that brews a spring-like love in the autumn season, a dream of a season.

But where has Linlin gone? Has Linlin’s heart changed with the autumn? I know Linlin’s heart is forever joyful and carefree.

Because Linlin is a little sparrow suited to living under the warm sunshine.

But the wanderer's journey and the desert-like state of mind, a heart as desolate as the desert, and a joyful heart are separated by heavy mountains and heavy seas.

Happy times have sunk like shooting stars in the sky. Linlin, the appointment to meet again after three autumns is now more than three years overdue. Perhaps this appointment will become an eternal regret. The fate of iron ore cannot produce beautiful fruit. Besides indulging in dream-like intoxication with lingering tears in my dreams, what else can I hope for? I am already prepared to silently chew on the bitterness of life, carrying the cross of crucifixion, and from now on destroy all the yearnings in the world. Only you, Linlin, your face on the gray screen of my heart will never wither, forever an immortal statue of the soul. However, I wish you to be joyful, to live joyfully under the warm sunshine of the South, joyfully.

I don't want you to wither your youth too quickly because of worry and sorrow, Linlin!

These long days, this long wandering life, I have no feeling, no joy, not even fantasy. Every day is the same! Watching the sun rise and sink, listening to my own sunset dirge with the sound of time, silently passing from my heart, from my ears, passing by, I have not a single feeling. I just sigh silently, sighing. Autumn in the South is lovely. But autumn can only give me a degree of sadness. Linlin, what about you?

Self-Employment Introductions 219

A certain Mr. Qun, 21 years old, from Shanghai, with a middle school education, is now seeking positions as a clerk, assistant, office worker, or trainee. He has a solid shop as collateral and two hundred yuan in cash as security. If formal companies, agencies, or firms need such talent, please send letters to Mr. Lu Qiliang Qun, c/o Peiyu Elementary School, Binlang Road Intersection, Xiaoshadu Road.

Mr. Tong Jun, 32 years old, graduated from a certain university in an important port, and has held important military and political positions in various provinces. He is now willing to serve in a secondary school in this city. He can teach Chinese language, history, geography, military affairs, and politics. Contact address: c/o Mr. Jiang Shi, No. 65 Bailinan Road.

Mr. Yun, 19 years old, from Wuxian County, graduated from middle school and has served as a clerk in a cultural institution and a primary school teacher. He is now willing to take up the above positions or work as a senior trainee or assistant copyist in banks, companies, or foreign firms. Those who wish to employ him please write to No. 126 Xinchang Lane, Beishi Road.

Ms. Xia, 20 years old, from Shanghai, with a middle school education, has served as a clerk and office worker in a large national goods company. She is now willing to take up the above positions, as well as positions as office workers in agencies, companies, and foreign firms. Those who wish to employ her please write to Ms. Wang Yunxia, c/o Shanghai National Goods Company, Nanjing Road.

Fiction

Uncle's Braid (9) 220

— Ling He

Upon investigation, it was indeed correct. That evening, Magistrate Rui ordered a coffin to be bought and placed in the main hall. He ordered that Yue official to lie down in it, and then ordered other military officers to cut a knife into his chest. He then covered the coffin and had it carried away and buried overnight.

Thinking of this, Xu Zhai lightly closed his eyes, as if the bloody appearance of that Yue official was right in front of him. However, now the strict Magistrate Rui, who commanded the army, has now fled to a foreign warship. Such awe-inspiring figures have also met with such an end. Xu Zhai picked up the newspaper again to read:

It is heard that the hearts of the soldiers of Admiral Sa’s fleet are very unstable. When firing the cannons, the cannons all fired into the sky, and no revolutionaries were injured or killed. Therefore, the fleet has docked downstream. There is a small gunboat whose soldiers have all surrendered to the revolution. The ship is currently docked near Jiujiang because it cannot navigate elsewhere.

Tang Hualong telegraphed to the Beijing Diplomatic Corps and the Customs Service to request them to send personnel to observe the battle.

Yesterday, an imperial conference was held, followed by a secret order to the Governor of Shaanxi to properly arrange matters in Xi'an.

Yuan Shikai telegraphed a memorial requesting permission to lead troops forward on the second day of the ninth month, with Duan Zhigui as the commander of the advance troops, and presented six strategies for quelling the rebellion. The Emperor approved with praise and ordered him to quickly advance to comfort the court's worries.

A certain censor memorialized that the situation is critical, the military expenses are huge, and the treasury is depleted. He requested that internal funds be issued to encourage the morale of the troops.

Governor Rui hid on a foreign warship and fled the city. The court ordered Yuan Shikai to handle the situation as he sees fit.

Beijing officials are fleeing Beijing one after another.

The United States has proposed that the success of the revolution in Hubei will spread to other provinces, and the war cannot be ended in a short time. Moreover, it is feared that after the revolution spreads, its leaders may not be able to restrain themselves adequately, which will lead to anti-foreign sentiment, greatly affecting the property and interests of foreigners in China. The whole world believes that this revolution will overthrow the government and expel the Manchus. If this step is taken, when China's diplomacy with various countries is not yet settled, if the various countries do not pre-negotiate a common policy and a method to respond to changes, international disputes will inevitably arise. The United States has initiated this matter in order to protect the interests of China and foreigners. The United States not only has no intention of interfering, but also wants to prevent other countries from interfering arbitrarily. If a country is compelled to interfere, it must not do so without the fair consent of all countries.

On the twenty-eighth day of the eighth month, the Cabinet received an imperial edict from the Regent, Prince Regent, and Empress Dowager Longyu, stating that the southern provinces have been repeatedly flooded recently, and this year there are bandits rebelling in Hubei. Considering the hunger and distress of the refugees who have lost their homes, We deeply sympathize with them and are eager to provide relief. Now, 200,000 taels of silver will be allocated from the internal funds in the palace left by Empress Xiaoling Xian. The Ministry of Internal Affairs will hand it over to Yuan Shikai to appoint suitable personnel to verify the situation in the Hubei area and provide relief to the disaster victims. Respect this.
